Introduction to Sulam Commentary



Chapter 1

<b>The Ten <i>Sefirot</i></b><br>1. <b>First, one must know the names of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>. They are KḤB, ḤGT, NHYM, which are acronyms for</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>;</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>;</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. These constitute the ten coverings of God’s light, which were established so that the lower beings could receive His light. This can be compared to the light of the sun, which can be viewed only through tinted lenses, which reduce its light and render it suitable for the eyes’ faculty of sight. Likewise, though on a vastly different plane, the lower beings would be unable to apprehend God’s light were it not covered by these ten coverings called the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, for the lower</b> the <i>sefira</i><b>, the more it obscures God’s light.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">In this last point, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> is explaining why there are ten <i>sefirot</i> as opposed to only one. One <i>sefira</i> would not be sufficient to obscure God’s light, so each additional covering provides greater cover, reducing God’s light to a level that is comprehensible to the lower, created beings. Each subsequent <i>sefira</i> in the list is considered “lower” than the preceding <i>sefirot</i>, reflecting a greater distance from the supernal light and an increased obscuring of the light. </i>

Chapter 2

2. <b>These ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>are the mystical meaning of the ten holy names in the Torah: The name <i>Eheyeh</i> represents the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>; the name <i>Yah</i> is the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>; the Tetragrammaton,</b> the four-letter name of God, <b>with the vowels of</b> the name<i> <b>Elohim</b></i><b>, is <i></i></b><i><b>Bina</b></i><b>; the name <i>El</i> is <i>Ḥesed</i>; the name <i>Elohim</i> is</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>; the Tetragrammaton with the vowels <i>sheva</i>, <i>ḥolam</i>, and <i>kamatz</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The Tetragrammaton is a word that is not pronounced as it is lettered. Accordingly, the particular pronunciation of the written Tetragrammaton will depend on the assigned vowels, and this varies depending on the Oral Tradition of the Torah's vowels. </i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>; the name <i>Tzeva’ot</i> is</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>; the name <i>Shaddai</i> is</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>; and the name <i>Adonai</i> is</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>(as stated in the <i>Zohar</i>,<i> Vayikra </i>157–163, 166–177).</b>

Chapter 3

3. <b>Even though we count ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, they constitute no more than five</b> <b>levels</b><b>, which are called</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. The characteristics</b> of the <i>sefirot</i> <b>are fully explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i> (<i>Introduction to the Wisdom of the Kabbala</i>)<b>, from the beginning until section 7.</b> It is advisable to <b>see the detailed</b> discussion there<b>. Consequently, there is no need to repeat that lengthy exposition here,</b> even <b>though that</b> work contains <b>the foundation of the wisdom of <i>Kabbala</i></b> and so is worthy of study.
<b>The reason we count ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>is that the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>encompasses six</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, which are</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>. Accordingly, they amount to ten. The underlying reasoning for</b> this structure <b>is discussed in the Introduction to the <i>Zohar</i>, in the</b> <i><b>Marot HaSulam</b></i> <b>commentary (p. 5). These five</b> <b>levels</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, can be discerned in every emanated being and each creation. This</b> parallelism <b>applies to the totality of all the worlds, which are five worlds known as</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i> (Primordial Man)<b>,</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> (Emanation), <i><b>Beria</b></i> (Creation), <i><b>Yetzira</b></i> (Formation), <b>and</b> <i><b>Asiya</b></i> (Actualization), <b>and which correspond to the five</b> <b>levels</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i>. The parallelism <b>applies equally to the smallest entity in existence, in which we can discern that its head is</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i>, <b>from its head to the chest is</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, from the chest to the navel is</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and from the navel and below is</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Here, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> references the notion that every entity in existence has an underlying structure formed of the <i>sefirot</i>. The <i>sefirot</i> are the foundation for a more complex structure called a <i>partzuf</i>, which is described as having a head and body parts that correspond to different <i>sefirot</i>.</i> <b>The topic of the five worlds is explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i> <b>(see sections 6–10).</b>

Chapter 4

<b>Why</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>Encompasses</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><br>4. <b>When the five</b> <b>levels</b> <b>–</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>– emerged</b> into existence<b>, they incorporated one another, such that each of them, individually, was comprised of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. However, within the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, the structures of the</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>descended from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the first three.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Each of the five <i>sefirot</i> are individually composed of all (the same) five <i>sefirot</i>. The point here is that the five <i>sefirot</i> that make up the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Tiferet</i> are lower than the <i>sefirot</i> making up the previous <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and <i>Bina</i> (called “the first three”). The reason for this lower state is that the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Tiferet</i> primarily shines the light of giving (<i>ḥassadim</i>), while the previous, higher three levels shine the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> (wisdom). As a result, the five <i>sefirot</i> that make up <i>Tiferet</i> are given different names, indicating their lower position. The author expands this point in the following lines.</i> <b>Consequently, within the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, the names</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which are incorporated in each of the five</b> <b>levels</b><b>, have been changed to</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Tiferet</i> contains an additional <i>sefira</i> called <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, which incorporates them all. Therefore, when we say that</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>encompasses six</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, this is not due to the elevated status of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>over the first three</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. Rather, it is due to the deficiency</b> of <i>Tiferet</i> <b>with respect to the light of the first three that the five</b> <b>levels</b> <b>within</b> <i>Tiferet</i> <b>–</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>– received other names, which are</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>Thus,</b> in the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. They are joined by the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, which is not another</b> <b>level</b> <b>in addition to the five</b> <b>levels</b><b>, but rather it is simply an encompassing</b> <b>level</b><b>, since it incorporates within it all five</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>. These</b> six <i>sefirot</i> <b>are invariably identified</b> by the acronym <b><i>VAK</i>, which is an acronym for <i>vav ketzavot</i>,</b> or six extremities, <b>which are these six</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">The six extremities refer to the six directional edges or limits of every physical being: above, below, right, left, front, and back. These six extremities correspond to the six <i>sefirot</i> that represent the body of a <i>partzuf</i>: <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i>, <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i>. </i> <b>Since this descent of the five</b> <b>levels</b> <b>to</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> <b>occurs only in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, we attribute these five changed</b> <b>levels</b> <b>only to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> will explain in the following sections, the <i>sefirot</i> are the foundation for spiritual structures called <i>partzufim</i>. There are five <i>partzufim</i> types, and each corresponds to one of the five levels discussed here. The level of <i>Tiferet</i> corresponds to the <i>partzuf</i> called <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>, which is the reason the author of the <i>Sulam</i> writes here that the lower forms of the five <i>sefirot</i> making up <i>Tiferet</i> are associated with this <i>partzuf</i>.</i>

Chapter 5

<b>Light and Vessel</b><br>5. <b>It is impossible for light to exist in all the worlds without a vessel. The concept of a spiritual vessel is explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, sections 3 and 4. Initially, there was only one vessel in the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, which was</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. When we say that there are five</b> <b>levels</b><b>, namely,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, all these are all only parts of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which is called the</b> <b>fourth</b> <b>level</b><b>. In other words,</b> these <i>sefirot</i> <b>are defined according to their position in the process of the completion of the vessel, which is the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that is called the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 5). However, after the</b> <b>first constriction</b> (<i>tzimtzum</i>), <b>a</b> <b>partition</b> <b>was placed upon the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, blocking the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>from being</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in it. Therefore, when the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>reaches the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>collides with the light and rebuffs it. This collision is referred to as the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>against the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>upon the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. The light that is rebuffed backward is called the “ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>,” since the light that is rebuffed ascends from below to above and</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>that are in the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>, known as the “ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light.” New vessels are formed from this</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>to</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>, replacing</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which was constricted so that it could not receive light. The content of those new vessels, which are called the “ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>,” is explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i> <b>sections 14–26.</b>

Chapter 6

<b>Head, Interior, End ; Mouth, Navel, Endpoint of the Legs</b> of the <i>partzuf</i><br>6. <b>On account of the new vessels</b> formed <b>from the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>, we can discern three aspects in each</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. These are called</b> <b>head</b><b>, interior, and end.</b> The end of section 5 above <b>explained that the resistive force of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>preventing the arrival of the light</b> in the vessel <b>of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>led to a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>with the light</b> against the partition. As a result, <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>emerged and</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light that is the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">“Direct light” and “supernal light” refer to the same divine light. The discussion here is analogous to a discussion of water, and the molecules of H2O that are “within” the water. Those molecules actually <i>are</i> the water, but sometimes we speak of water in its unity (calling it, simply, “water”), while at other times, we speak of water in terms of its more granular structure. When the author of the <i>Sulam</i> seeks to emphasize the unity of the divine light, he refers to it as “supernal light.” Yet, there is a structure of <i>sefirot</i> vessels undergirding that supernal light. When describing this more discrete perspective of the divine light, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> uses the term “direct light.”</i> <b>These ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>and the direct light are called the “ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>.”</b>
<b>However, these ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>, which emerge from the</b> <b>partition</b> and rise <b>upward and which</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light, are not yet genuine vessels, because the term “vessel” is indicative of</b> <b>opacity</b><b>, namely, the force of judgment that the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>contains, which prevents the</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the light in</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. There is a principle that the force of judgment is active only from the place where the judgment is located and below</b> it, <b>not from the place where the judgment is located and above</b> it.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">The force of judgment in a level derives from the particular amount of will to receive found within that level. This will to receive cannot operate above its own level. In kabbalistic thought, “lower level“ denotes an increase in limitations and finitude, as the concepts of barriers and containment are increasingly manifested. These concepts are expressive of the force of judgment, as judgment is the dynamic of delineation, selectivity, standards, and evaluations. Accordingly, the “amount” of judgment that exists in a particular level derives from the “amount” of the will to receive that is unique to that level. As a result, the force of judgment in a level cannot operate above that level, since the will to receive of the level is unique to the level and would be reduced in the higher level above. </i> <b>Since the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>emerged from the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>and</b> rose <b>upward, as stated above, the force of judgment is therefore not discernible in the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>,</b> and the returning light <b>is not fit to be a</b> genuine <b>vessel.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> explains, in order to be a true vessel, opacity is required. Thus, the returning light cannot serve as a true vessel, since it is “above” the partition. However, the returning light and its vessels serve as roots, theoretical forms of the fully formed vessels that manifest below the partition as the body. As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> elucidates, the theoretical vessel structure above the partition is called the head.</i> <b>Consequently, the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>are called</b> <b>head</b><b>, which means the root of the vessels but not actual vessels.</b>
<b>In addition, the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>upon which the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>was placed for the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>is called</b> <b>mouth</b><b>. This alludes to the fact that just as in a corporeal mouth the letters emerge by means of a fusion through collision of the five</b> kinds of <b>utterances of the mouth, so too there is a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>in the spiritual mouth through which the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>emerge, which are the aforementioned five</b> <b>levels</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Here, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> employs an analogy to explain why the <i>Malkhut</i> of the head of the <i>partzuf</i> is called the mouth. The mouth of the body operates to convey the intangible world of a person’s thoughts into the more tangible form of audible words. Words are compiled out of combinations of letters, which serve as “vessels” to carry our thoughts into the world, where they can be received by others. Letters serve as containers, which are inherently limiting, hence why we often misunderstand each other in verbal communication. Additionally, the formation of letters with our mouths involves the shaping of the sounds emanating from our throats through the impacting of the different parts of the mouth with each other. This is the meaning of the “fusion through collision” that we have in our mouths, analogous to the fusion through collision in the mouth of the <i>partzuf</i>. The fusion through collision in the mouth of the <i>partzuf</i> gives rise to the fully formed vessels of the body of the <i>partzuf</i>, which can then contain the supernal light. It is this containment that allows the supernal light to be experienced by finite beings like us, just like the containment power of letters allows our own inner worlds to be experienced by those around us.</i> <b>These</b> emerging <i>sefirot</i> of the returning light <b>are the vessels of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light, and the vessels are</b> therefore <b>referred to as letters.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">The five vessels of the <i>sefirot</i> are analogous to the five parts of the mouth used for verbal articulation. They are the throat, palate, teeth, tongue, and lips. The flow of sound travels through these five “levels” and collides with them, forming the letters.</i> <b>This is the explanation of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 7

7. <b>Therefore,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">This point returns to the middle of the previous section , explaining the logic as to why the returning light was only able to serve as complete vessels for the direct light below the partition and not above it.</i> <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light and the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>had to spread from the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>and downward.</b> The reason is that <b>it was at that point that the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>became vessels that receive and</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light. At this stage, the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>is already</b> positioned <b>above the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>, and therefore its</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>controls the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>returning light</b><b>, and it is through this</b> positioning <b>that they are formed into vessels.</b>
<b>These ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, which are formed into actual vessels, are termed “interior” and “</b><b>body</b><b>“, meaning that they are the inner part, the inside, and the exterior, the body, of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. The</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the interior is termed “navel,” as in the phrase “the navel</b> [<i>tabur</i>] <b>of the earth,”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Ezekiel 38:12.</i> <b>which means the center, the middle. This indicates that the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the interior is the central</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, from which its</b> <b>returning light</b><b>, the actualized vessels of the</b> <b>body</b><b>, were made. It can further be stated that</b> the word for navel<b>,<i> tabur</i>, comes from the letters of <i>tov or</i>,</b> “good light,” <b>indicating that the light is “good” up to that point since it is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessels that are suitable for receiving it. This is the explanation of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior until the navel.</b>

Chapter 8

8. <b>There are two aspects of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>:</b>
1. <b>The</b> first is the <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b><b>, which refers to the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>preventing the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>from being</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.</b>
2. <b>The</b> second is the <b>fusing <i>Malkhut</i></b><b>, for were it not for the fusion of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>with the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, in the mystical phenomenon of the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, which gives rise to the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>in order to</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>, the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>would not have receiving vessels and there would be no light within reality, for there is no light without vessels, as stated above.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See section 5.</i>
<b>In the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>these two aspects are present only in the form of two roots. The</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> of the head <b>is the root of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> of the body <b>that ends the</b> <b>level</b><b>, while the</b> <b>fusing <i>Malkhut</i></b> of the head <b>is the root of the</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the light in the vessels.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The partition that rests upon <i>Malkhut</i> has two functions. It prevents the supernal light from entering <i>Malkhut</i>, and also fuses with the supernal light to create the returning light. These two features are called the terminating <i>Malkhut</i> and the fusing <i>Malkhut</i>, respectively. They appear in the head of the <i>partzuf</i> in a “root” (theoretical) form, but then manifest fully in the body of the <i>partzuf</i>. The fusing <i>Malkhut</i> aspect is expressed in the body as the area from the mouth of the <i>partzuf</i> until the navel, as there, the supernal light is enclothed (an expression of “fusion”) in the <i>partzuf</i>. From the navel downward, the aspect of the terminating <i>Malkhut</i> is manifest. The terminating <i>Malkhut</i>, another set of ten <i>sefirot</i>, is the conclusion of the <i>partzuf</i>, marking the end of the level of existence represented by the particular <i>partzuf</i>. In this lower area, the supernal light is almost completely blocked out (an expression of “termination”).</i> <b>These two dynamics become manifest and occur in the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>: From the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>to the navel is where the force of the</b> <b>fusing <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>is apparent since the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessels. From the navel and downward, the force of the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>is apparent and produces the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end</b> of the <i>partzuf</i><b>, in which each</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>emerges only with the illumination of the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>without</b> the illumination of <b>the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>. At the point of the</b> <i>sefira</i> of <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of these ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end, each</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>is terminated because this</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>that does not receive anything, and therefore the spreading</b> supernal light that is within <b>the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>is arrested there</b> from continuing to lower levels.<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>sefirot</i> of the bottom part of the <i>partzuf</i> contain the aspect of the terminating <i>Malkhut</i>, and thus block the supernal light from entering the bottom area. The last <i>sefira</i> of the set of ten <i>sefirot</i> comprising this area is that of <i>Malkhut</i>. This <i>Malkhut</i> can be thought of as the embodiment of the terminating <i>Malkhut</i> (as explained in <i>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</i><i>,</i> section 50), and therefore, at that point in the structure, the <i>partzuf</i> is “terminated,” and ends. </i> <b>We call this “the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the end of the legs,”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the end of the lower “extremities” of the <i>partzuf</i>, the bottom edge of its conceptual structure.</i> <b>which cuts the light and arrests the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> from continuing<b>. These ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end, which spread from the navel and downward, to the end of the legs, are called “ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end” because they are all parts of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the end and the conclusion.</b> However, <b>when we say that these</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>contain only</b> <b>returning light</b><b>, this does not mean that they contain none of the direct light. Rather, it means that they also contain a small illumination from the direct light, but this is considered</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>without a</b> <b>head</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">The concept of the six extremities refers to a level characterized by the lower <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>. As is explained here, this type of level is primarily illuminated with the light of giving (<i>ḥassadim</i>), and only slightly illuminated by the direct light, the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. It is thus described as being “six extremities without a head,” like a body that lacks a mind to animate it. The number six refers to the six lower <i>sefirot</i> of the level of <i>Tiferet</i> mentioned in section 4 above. In contrast, the levels characterized by higher <i>partzufim</i> are primarily illuminated by the direct light, the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. These levels are called the “first three,” referring to the first three <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Bina</i>, and the <i>partzufim</i> that are associated with them.</i> <b>See </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, sections 50–53.</b>

Chapter 9

<b>Chest</b><br>9. <b>Up to this point, we have discussed the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>. However, in the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, a new end point is added to the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior: the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the interior, which is called “navel,” rises to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior, where it forms an endpoint for the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the interior.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Here, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> introduces the concept of the second constriction, which applies only from the level of the world of <i>Nekudim</i> and the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> which derives from it, and downward. In this process, the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Malkhut</i> that was positioned at the navel, the bottom of the interior aspect of the <i>partzuf</i>, is repositioned to the chest of the <i>partzuf</i>, the place of the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Bina</i>. This changes the format of the <i>partzuf</i> such that the interior area now ends at the point of the chest (just as <i>Malkhut</i> of the navel marked the end of the interior before the repositioning). Additionally, the area below the chest now becomes part of the lower area of the <i>partzuf</i> that was below the navel. The chest thus acts as a new separation, a new endpoint, wherein only two <i>sefirot</i> of the interior, <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and half of the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Bina</i>, remain above the chest, in the interior. The remaining <i>sefirot</i> of the interior “fall” below the separation, into the area of the end of the <i>partzuf</i>, with the six extremities. This second constriction is integral to the purpose of Creation, as the author of the <i>Sulam</i> will explain.</i> <b>This endpoint is called “chest.”</b>
<b>A diaphragm is thus inserted there. In other words, the new end point that was formed on account of the ascension of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, in the place</b> called <b>the chest, is called “diaphragm”</b> based <b>on the mystical meaning of the firmament that separates between the upper waters, which are</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which remained within the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the interior, and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which were ejected from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior and became the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">The author of the <i>Sulam</i> explains here that the Torah alludes to this separating diaphragm in Genesis 1:7. The repositioning of <i>Malkhut</i> from the navel at the bottom of the interior to the level of <i>Bina</i> at the chest, effectively “partnering” <i>Malkhut</i> with <i>Bina</i>, causes the levels of <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> to be separated from <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i>. <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i> are the “waters” that lie above the firmament, and <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> are the “waters” below. </i> <b>Because of this diaphragm, the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior were divided into two</b> <b>levels</b><b>:</b> The area <b>from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>to the chest is considered the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior,</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, and the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>; from the chest and downward, to the navel is considered the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end,</b> the level of <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>, and the six extremities without a</b> <b>head</b><b>, like the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end. With regard to the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and the new endpoint that occurs in the middle of every</b> <b>level</b><b>, see sections 15 and 16 below.</b>

Chapter 10

<b>The Inverse Relationship between Vessels and Lights</b> <br>10. <b>There is a consistent inverse relationship between the lights and the vessels. In the case of the vessels, it is the higher vessels that develop first in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. First</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>enters the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, then</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, then</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, then</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and then</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. This is why we list the vessels in the order of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, </b><i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, that is, from highest to lowest, since that is the order of their entrance into the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>The reverse is the case with regard to the lights since the order of the lights is that the lower ones enter the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>first. Initially the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>enters</b> the <i>partzuf</i>, <b>then the light of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, then the light of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>, then the light of</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and then the light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>. Thus, the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>enters first, which is the light of</b> the vessel of <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, the smallest of all the lights, and at the end, the light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>enters</b> the <i>partzuf</i>, <b>which is the largest of all the lights. Consequently, we list the lights in the order of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, that is, from lowest to highest, since that is the order of their entrance into the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 11

11. <b>Accordingly, when there is only one vessel in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, which is necessarily the highest vessel,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> which is <b>the vessel that develops first, then the largest light, the one that is linked to</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, will not enter the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. Rather, the smallest light, which is the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>, will enter</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>and will be</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>When two vessels have developed in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, which are the two largest ones, that is,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>also enters</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>and the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> then <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>to the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the light of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>In this manner, when a third vessel has developed in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, which is the vessel of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i> <b>enters the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, and then the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to the vessel of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>leaves the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and enters the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the light of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i> <b>is then</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>When a fourth vessel has developed in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, which is the vessel of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i> <b>enters the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, and then the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>to the vessel of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> descends <b>to the vessel of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i> descends <b>to the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the light of</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i> is enclothed <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>When a fifth vessel has developed in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, which is the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, all the lights enter the vessels to which they are related. The light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>is drawn into the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, and the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>to the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>and enters the vessel of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i> <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and enters the vessel of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the light of</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i> <b>descends from the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and enters the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>enters and is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 12

12. <b>You thus find that as long as all five vessels –</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>– have not developed in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, the lights are not in their appropriate places. What is more, they maintain an inverse relationship, for if the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, the smallest vessel, is absent in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, the largest light,</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, is missing. If the two lowest vessels,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, are absent, the two highest lights,</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> and <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, will be missing. If the three lowest vessels,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, are absent, the three highest lights,</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>, will be missing, and so on in this manner. As long as all five vessels –</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>– have not developed in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, there will be an inverse relationship between the vessels and the lights: If one light and one vessel are lacking, then with regard to the lights, the largest light, which is the light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, will be missing, while the reverse is the case for the vessels. The smallest vessel will be missing, which is the vessel of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, in the manner described above.</b>

Chapter 13

13. <b>With this in mind, you will understand what we are saying: that through the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the</b> <b>level</b> <b>ends under</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and for this reason only two</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>remain in the</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, while</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>are negated and descend from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>(as will be explained below in section 17).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Every level is built out the five <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i>. After the second constriction, the <i>Malkhut</i>, which is the end of a given level, moved up and connected to <i>Bina</i>, moving the “end” of that level upward under <i>Ḥokhma</i>, inside the <i>Bina</i>. This movement essentially ejects the lower vessels <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i>, and <i>Malkhut</i> of a given level from that level, “negating” them from their previous placement. Because of this change, from the moment of the second constriction, every level is left with two vessels of <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and two lights of <i>nefesh</i> and <i>ruaḥ</i>.</i> <b>Now this applies only from the perspective of the vessels, but from the perspective of the lights the reverse is the case. The lights of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>remain in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, while the lights of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>are negated from the</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 14

14. <b>With this in mind, you will understand how the <i>Zohar</i> will sometimes state that with the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>the five letters of the name <i>Elohim</i></b> (<i>alef-lamed-heh-yod-mem</i>) <b>were divided in such a manner that the two letters <i>mem </i></b>and<i> <b>yod</b></i><b> remained in the <i></i></b><b>level</b><b>, while the three letters <i>alef</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and<i> <b>heh</b></i><b> left and were negated from the <i></i></b><b>level</b> <b>(as explained in the Introduction to the <i>Zohar</i>, p. 20, in the <i>Sulam </i>, s.v. “<i>tziyer</i>”).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">The “ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i>“ refers to the second constriction mentioned previously, in which <i>Malkhut</i> ascends from the end of a given level up to the level of <i>Bina</i>, connecting with <i>Bina</i> and creating a new endpoint in the level.</i> <b>On other occasions, the <i>Zohar</i> will say the converse, that with the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>the five letters of the name <i>Elohim</i> were divided in such a manner that the two letters <i>alef </i></b>and <b><i>lamed </i>remained in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, while the three letters <i>heh</i>,<i> mem</i>,</b> and <b><i>yod</i> were negated and descended from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>(as explained in the <i>Zohar</i>, <i>Bereshit</i> 1:59).</b>
<b>The idea</b> that the <i>Zohar</i> is conveying <b>is that the five letters of <i>Elohim</i> represent the mystical meaning of the five vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, and the five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>. With the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, from the perspective of the vessels</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>remained in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, which correspond to the two letters <i>alef</i></b> and <b><i>lamed</i>, while the three letters <i>heh</i>,<i> yod</i>,</b> and <b><i>mem</i> descended from the</b> <b>level</b><b>. Conversely, from the perspective of the lights, the two final letters, <i>mem </i></b>and<i> <b>yod</b></i><b>, which allude to the two lowest lights, <i></i></b><i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, are the ones that remained in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, whereas the three initial letters, <i>alef</i>, <i>lamed</i>, and <i>heh</i>, which allude to</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>, are the ones that left and were negated from the</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b>
<b>Accordingly, in the <i>Zohar</i>’s introduction, the <i>Zohar</i> is speaking of the five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, which are hinted at by the five letters of <i>Elohim</i>. It therefore states that <i>mem</i></b> and <b><i>yod</i> remained and <i>alef</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and <b><i>heh</i> left the</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b> On the other hand, <b>in <i>Bereshit</i>,</b> volume <b>1, the <i>Zohar</i> is discussing the five vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which are</b> also <b>alluded to by the five letters of <i>Elohim</i>. Consequently, it states the converse, that <i>alef </i></b>and <b><i>lamed</i> remained in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, while the three letters <i>heh</i>, <i>yod</i>,</b> and <b><i>mem</i> left the</b> <b>level</b><b>. These observations must be kept in mind, and one must consider on each occasion whether the reference is to the lights or the vessels, and this will resolve many apparent contradictions.</b>

Chapter 15

<b>The Ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <br>15. <b>It is important to fully understand the concept of the tempering of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is the root of the whole wisdom</b> of <i>Kabbala</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">The wisdom of the <i>Kabbala</i> describes the formation and governing of the higher and lower worlds. The ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> is a fundamental conceptual component of this process. This ascent acts as the driver of these formations, the myriad structures that comprise the worlds of <i>Atzilut</i>, <i>Beria</i>, <i>Yetzira</i> and <i>Asiya</i> and their contents. </i> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is the mystical meaning of the attribute of judgment through which the world cannot exist.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">After the first constriction, <i>Malkhut</i>, which is the will to receive, was unable to directly receive the supernal light. As a result, <i>Malkhut</i> operates as a force that limits the light and imposes darkness upon the vessels. This limiting dynamic is the “attribute of judgement” discussed here. In contrast, <i>Bina</i> represents the “will to bestow,” which is not affected by the first constriction and is not a force that limits the supernal light. The limiting force of <i>Malkhut</i> is described in <i>Kabbala</i> as a harsh force, blocking out the supernal light. As a result, the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> is meant to temper that harshness by mixing together the limiting force of <i>Malkhut</i> with the bestowing dynamic of <i>Bina</i>.</i> <b>Therefore, the Creator</b> raised <i>Malkhut</i> <b>to the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is the attribute of mercy. The Sages alluded to this idea: “Initially it was</b> God’s <b>intent to create the world through the attribute of judgment,” that is, through</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>alone, which is the attribute of judgment. “When He saw that the world could not exist</b> with the attribute of judgment alone, <b>He preceded</b> it with <b>the attribute of mercy, partnering it with the attribute of judgment” (<i>Bereshit Rabba</i>, end of 12). Through the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>receives the form of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is the attribute of mercy, and then</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>directs the world through the attribute of mercy.</b>
<b>This ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>occurs in each and every</b> <b>level</b><b>, from the beginning of the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>until the end of the world of</b> <i><b>Asiya</b></i><b>. There is no</b> <b>level</b> <b>that does not contain ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>:</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. The</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that is in every</b> <b>level</b> <b>ascended to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>in that</b> <b>level</b> <b>and was tempered there.</b>

Chapter 16

<b>The Division of Each</b> <b>Level</b> <b>into Two Halves</b> <br>16. <b>It is known that</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>arrests</b> the light of <b>each</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>and every</b> <b>level</b><b>. In other words,</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>arrests the light in the</b> <b>level</b> <b>from spreading into</b> <i>Malkhut</i> <b>itself. This</b> arresting force <b>derives from the force of the</b> <b>constriction</b> <b>that was placed on</b> <i>Malkhut</i>, <b>so that it cannot receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>. Therefore, the light of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is drawn forth only up until</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. When</b> the light <b>reaches the</b> <b>partition</b> that is <b>upon</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>it is arrested, at which point a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>occurs with the light on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>that is on</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 14).</b>
<b>Consequently, since the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>ascended to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>in that same</b> <b>level</b><b>, the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>arrested the light in the place to which it ascended, that is, in the middle of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">This ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> is referred to as the second constriction, and is referred to in <i>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</i>, sections 57 – 58.</i> <b>The half of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which are situated under the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b><b>,</b> which is now situated in <i>Bina</i>, <b>left their</b> original <b>level</b> <b>and became a</b> separate, <b>second</b> <b>level</b> <b>under</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. Thus, on account of the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i>, <b>each</b> <b>level</b> <b>has been divided in half, so that</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and half of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which are above</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, remained in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, while half of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>(which contains</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>), and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>left the</b> <b>level</b> <b>and became the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below it. This blockage performed by</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>in the middle of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>is called a diaphragm</b>. <b>Keep this in mind.</b>

Chapter 17

17. <b>Each</b> <b>level</b> <b>is meant to contain five lights, which are called</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>. These are</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in five vessels called</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>(which contains</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>), and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. Since, on account of the ascent of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, only two whole vessels are left in the</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, while three vessels,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, are missing from it, only two of the lights remain,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, which are</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the two vessels of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, while the three lights of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>are missing from it, since they have no vessels in which they may be</b> <b>enclothed</b><b>.</b>
<b>It turns out that the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is lacking</b> the lights <b>of the first three</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, since on account of the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is cleaved into two halves: Half of it remains in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, namely the vessels</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and the lights</b> <b>ruaḥ</b> <b>and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>, while half of it left the</b> <b>level</b><b>, specifically the vessels</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>and the lights</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>Therefore, this ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>is alluded to through the mystical meaning of the <i>yod</i> that enters the <i>or</i>,</b> light (spelled <i>alef-vav-resh</i>) <b>of the</b> <b>level</b><b>, so that <i>or</i> becomes <i>avir</i>,</b> air (spelled <i>alef-vav-yod-resh</i>). <b>Due to the ascent of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the</b> <b>level</b> <b>lost the light of its first three</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>and remained at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>, which is called air (as explained in</b> <i>Zohar</i>, <b><i>Bereshit</i> 1:32, and in the <i>Sulam </i></b>there<b>, s.v. “<i>beka</i>”).</b>
<b>This concept is also hinted at in the five letters of the name <i>Elohim</i></b> (<i>alef-lamed-heh-yod-mem</i>), <b>which can be divided into two halves: <i>mi eleh</i></b> (<i>mem-yod</i>, and<i> alef-lamed-heh</i>), <b>so that the two letters of <i>mem </i></b>and <b><i>yod</i> allude to the two lights of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>, which are</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the two vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, that remained in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, while the three letters of <i>alef</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and <b><i>heh</i> allude to the three vessels that left the</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, as stated in section 14 above.</b>

Chapter 18

<b>The Descent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>to Its Place</b> <br>18. <b>However, through the ascent of the</b> <b>feminine waters</b><b>,</b> which stem <b>from the Torah and prayer of the lower creations, a supernal illumination is drawn forth from</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, which removes</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>in each</b> <b>level</b> <b>and lowers it to its place (as explained in</b> <i>Zohar</i>, <b><i>Vayak’hel</i> 41, s.v. “<i>vehe’arah</i>“). The three vessels,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, had previously left the</b> <b>level</b> <b>due to the entry of the <i>yod</i> (which is</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>) into the <i>or</i> (light) of the</b> <b>level</b><b>, which arrested the</b> <b>level</b> <b>under</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the <i>or</i>,</b> light, <b>became <i>avir</i>,</b> air; <b>Now, once</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>has descended from there and the <i>yod</i></b> (<i>Malkhut</i>) <b>has left <i>avir</i>, the vessels return to their</b> <b>levels</b><b>, and once again there are five vessels in the</b> <b>level</b><b>:</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. Since there are five vessels, all five lights –</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>– are</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in them once more, and the <i>avir</i> reverts to being <i>or</i>, as the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the first three</b> lights <b>has returned to the</b> <b>level</b><b>, and they are called <i>or</i>.</b>

Chapter 19

<b>A Phase of</b> <b>Immaturity</b> <b>and a Phase of</b> <b>Maturity</b> <br>19. <b>It has thus been explained that due to the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, two phases take place in each</b> <b>level</b><b>: a phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and a phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>. With the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i>Malkhut</i> <b>arrests the</b> <b>level</b> <b>there under</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>leave the</b> <b>level</b> <b>and enter the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below. Therefore, only the vessels of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and the lights of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>remain in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, and</b> the level <b>is</b> consequently <b>lacking the first three lights. This is the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>(as stated above in section 17).</b>
<b>After the lower creations raise the</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>and draw forth the illumination from</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, which removes</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the three vessels of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which fell to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below</b>, <b>return and ascend from there to their</b> <b>level</b> <b>as before. Since the five vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, are in their</b> <b>level</b><b>, the five lights,</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>, become</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in them once more (as stated above in section 18). This is the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b><b>. (It would be informative to refer to the Introduction to the <i>Zohar</i>, page 20, in the <i>Sulam </i>, s.v. “<i>tziyer</i>” where this idea is explained).</b>
<b>It has thus been explained that due to the falling of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from</b> their <b>level</b> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below, the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is in a state of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, that is, lacking in</b> the lights of <b>the first three, and through the return of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b><b>, the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is in a state of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, that is, with the filling of the first three</b> vessels with their respective lights.

Chapter 20

<b>How the Lower</b> Level <b>Ascends to Its Upper</b> Level <br>20. <b>By means of this ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the connection and the possibility for the ascent of each lower</b> level <b>to the</b> level <b>above it has been prepared.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">This section describes how a lower level can ascend to a higher level. In order for this ascent to take place, there must be an equating of form between the two levels (recall that in spiritual matters, an equating of form means connection and unification). Through the process of feminine waters which will be explained more extensively, the <i>Malkhut</i> leaves its position within <i>Bina</i>. This removal of <i>Malkhut</i> allows the displaced <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the higher level (the ones displaced by the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i>) to return to their higher place (the state of maturity). The important point added in this section is that while these displaced <i>sefirot</i> were in the lower state, they united with the <i>sefirot</i> of that lower level. When they subsequently return to their higher state, they remain united with those <i>sefirot</i> of the lower level, and they pull those isefirot</i> up with them. Thus, the ascent of feminine waters allows lower levels of existence to be elevated to higher levels. This elevated state further allows those lower levels to access amounts of supernal light and brains that would otherwise have been restricted to them in their lower state. <b>For there is a rule that an upper</b> level <b>which descends to the lower</b> level below <b>becomes like it, and likewise a lower</b> level <b>that ascends to the upper</b> level above <b>becomes like it. Therefore, when the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is in a state of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>– that is, when the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>ascends to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, expelling</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from that</b> <b>level</b> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below it – those</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>become one</b> <b>level</b> <b>with the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below it since the upper</b> level <b>that descends to the</b> level <b>below becomes like</b> the lower level.
<b>Consequently, when the</b> <b>level</b> <b>is in a state of</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>– that is, when</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>returns and leaves</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>and comes</b> back <b>to its place – and the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that fell from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>return to their</b> <b>level</b> <b>– they also take with them the lower</b> <b>level</b> <b>where they were residing at the time of their fall. Since they became a single</b> <b>level</b> <b>with the lower</b> level <b>at the time of their fall, and they became attached to it as one, they therefore also take it with them upon their return to the</b> higher <b>level</b><b>, raising the lower</b> <b>level</b> <b>to the higher</b> <b>level</b><b>. In accordance with the rule that a lower</b> <b>level</b> <b>that ascends to an upper</b> level <b>becomes like it, it follows that the lower</b> <b>level</b> <b>receives all the lights and</b> <b>brains</b> <b>that exist in the higher</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b>
<b>It has thus been explained how the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>brought about a connection between the</b> <b>levels</b><b>, so that each</b> <b>level</b> <b>can ascend to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>above it. Furthermore, even the lowest degree can ascend to the loftiest</b> <b>level</b> <b>through this connection that has been achieved through the falling of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from each</b> <b>level</b> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below it (as explained in <i>Sulam </i></b>on <i>Zohar</i>, <b><i>Vayak’hel</i> 41, s.v. “<i>vezeh amru</i>”).</b>

Chapter 21

<b>The Immature and Mature</b> States <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><br>21. <b>After explaining the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>in broad outlines, how it occurs in each and every</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the four worlds of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Asiya</b></i><b>, these matters will now be explained in detail. Let us take, as an example, the two</b> <b>levels</b> <b>called</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>that are in the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>. Due to the ascent of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, in the state of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, the three</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>left and fell to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, and these</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>became attached to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>at the time of their fall. Therefore, when the time of</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>arrived, when the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>reverted and left the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and came</b> back <b>to its place, so that</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>returned from their fall and came</b> back <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, they also raised</b> the level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>along with them, since they were attached to it at the time</b> when they were in the state <b>of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, when they fell. It thus follows that</b> the level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>also ascended and became</b> one with <b>the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, likewise receiving the same lights and</b> <b>brains</b> <b>that are fit for the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>.</b>

Chapter 22

<b>If not for the Ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>Would Not Be Fit for</b> brains<br>22. <b>At this stage, it should be understood that on their own,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>are unfit to receive the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>at all, because the source of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>is from below the navel of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i> <b>(see section 8 above). It is there that the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the attribute of judgment is dominant, and the force of the</b> first <b>constriction</b> <b>rests upon</b> that region<b>, and it is thus unfit to receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">As will be explained in the next sections and the accompanying footnotes, the area below the navel of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> referred to here represents an area of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> that has no access to the supernal light. At the point of the navel and below, the power of <i>Malkhut</i> is dominant. <i>Malkhut</i> cannot serve as a vessel for the supernal light because it is only will to receive, and has no capacity for giving, making it too different from the supernal light that is wholly giving. Therefore, any vessel that is within this area is restricted from receiving the supernal light.</i> <b>Now, however, when</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>have raised up the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>have become like the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, and they are able to receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>like</b> <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>.

Chapter 23

23. <b>Now the statement of the Sages</b> cited above <b>can be properly understood:</b><sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">See section 15.</i> <b>“Initially, it was</b> God’s <b>intent to create the world through the attribute of judgment” – that is, through the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>first constriction</b><b>, which is the attribute of judgment.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">fter the placement of the partition resulting from the first constriction, <i>Malkhut</i> was unable to directly receive the supernal light. As a result, <i>Malkhut</i> operates as a force that limits the light and imposes darkness upon the vessels. This limiting dynamic is the “attribute of judgement” discussed here.</i> <b>The term “world” should be explained as referring to the</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, which are called “world.” It can also be interpreted as referring to this world, which receives</b> supernal light <b>from the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, for everything that is received in</b> the level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>can be received by human beings in this world, whereas anything that is not received in the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>cannot be received by human beings in this world, as we cannot receive from</b> any level <b>above the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> in <i>Atzilut</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">This level of <i>Atzilut</i> can be thought of as a sort of divine root of our world. There are many levels that are higher than this level of <i>Atzilut</i>, but since they are beyond the root of our world, and similarly, beyond the root of our very selves, we have no way of accessing them. If we think of the different levels and layers as coverings or filters for the supernal light, then the intensity or radiance of the supernal light above this level of <i>Atzilut</i> is beyond our capacity. Only after it is filtered through this layer does it begin to reach states that are accessible to us. The root of our souls derives from <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>, the root of this world. </i> <b>Therefore, since the root of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>is below the navel of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, where the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the attribute of judgment is dominant,</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i><b>cannot receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>and continue to exist, on account of the constriction of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>which controls them. All the more so, this world cannot exist.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">At this point in the discussion, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> is addressing the state of things if there would not have been a second constriction, which is the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i>. He does so in order to substantiate the explanation of the words of the Sages regarding the partnering of judgment with mercy to create the world. The issue here is that the root in <i>Adam Kadmon</i> of the lower part of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>, which is <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>, is positioned below the navel of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. This area of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is the end of that higher <i>partzuf</i>, the area where the supernal light cannot enter. This means that the supernal light has no way of reaching <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>, which is the <i>partzuf</i> and level of <i>Atzilut</i> that is the root of our world. Accordingly, in this state, our world cannot exist, as it would have no access to the supernal light that provides lifeforce for existence. As the author of the Sulam goes on to explain, the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> allows for <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i> to ascend to the higher level of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, the roots of which are above the navel of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. It is this elevation that allows for our world to exist, as it allows <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i> to receive supernal light, and in turn, to transmit that light to the lower levels. </i>
<b>This is the meaning of</b> the continuation of <b>the statement</b> of the Sages: <b>“When He saw that the world could not exist</b> with the attribute of judgment alone, <b>He preceded</b> it with <b>the attribute of mercy, partnering it with the attribute of judgment.” This means that He raised up</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>which is the attribute of judgment, of every</b> <b>level</b><b>, to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>which is the attribute of mercy, of the</b> <b>level</b><b>. The</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>ascended to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, as a result of which</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, fell to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, and became attached to them. As a consequence, when the</b> level of <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>reached a state of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, where the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>reverted and descended from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>to its place, and the three vessels</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, returned to their place, to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, as before, they also took with them the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>that was attached to them. They raised them to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, and the</b> level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>became like the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, meaning they became fit to receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>like</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>(as stated in section 21 above). Accordingly,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and give to this world, and</b> only <b>now this world can exist. However, without the combination of the attribute of judgment with the attribute of mercy – that is, if the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>had not ascended to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>– then the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>would not have fallen to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, and there would have been no possibility of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>ascending to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. In that case, they would not have been able to receive the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>on behalf of the world, and the world could not exist. The ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>has</b> now <b>been explained.</b>

Chapter 24

<b>Rectification of Lines</b> <br>24. <b>Now in the first three</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, which are referred to as</b> <i><b>gulgalta</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ab</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, the</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>were on one line, one below the other. However, in the</b> <b>world of <i>Nekudim</i></b> (Points)<b>, which</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>from the navel and below, of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">This terminology refers to how different layers and <i>partzufim</i> are “positioned” relative to each other. The enclothing here means that the level of the world of <i>Nekudim</i> operates in the spiritual environment that is from the navel of the world of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> and downward. As was discussed previously, and as will be discussed further, a <i>partzuf</i> has a head, body and end. Each of these different areas of a <i>partzuf</i> have different dynamics with regards to the supernal light flowing through the <i>partzuf</i>. The point here is that the world of <i>Nekudim</i> only begins below the navel of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, while the previous <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> are all above the navel. This difference sets the stage for the discussion of the rectification of lines. </i> <b>a rectification of lines occurred in the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i>, <b>but not in the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>. In the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, a rectification of lines transpired in the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>as well.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">This section begins the discussion of the rectification of lines, a process resulting from the second constriction. In the previous section, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> explained that the second constriction caused <i>Malkhut</i>, the fourth level, to ascend and mix together with the second level, the level of <i>Bina</i>. Prior to the second constriction, the <i>sefirot</i> were said to be stacked in one column.
