The reason for this was that each <i>sefirot</i> structure had one partition upon the level of <i>Malkhut</i> to interact with the direct light, and therefore only one element of opacity from that <i>Malkhut</i> within the structure. This opacity gave rise to the returning light which served to enclothe the direct light, creating a single column or structure of contained light. After the second constriction, however, each structure of <i>sefirot</i> interacting with the direct light has two imprints of <i>Malkhut</i> and <i>Bina</i> (and therefore effectively two partitions), which generate two different columns of light. These two columns are called “lines,” and they also require a third column or line to mediate between them.</i>

Chapter 25

<b>Two Aspects of the Rectification of Lines</b><br>25. <b>The underlying reasoning is that the rectification of lines that occurred in the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>results from the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, becoming the female to</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, so that as a result two sides were formed in the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">The concept of “female” in Kabbalistic thought is that of a vessel, possessing limits and boundaries. The ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> intermingles elements of the limitations and judgments found in <i>Malkhut</i> as a result of the first constriction within <i>Malkhut</i>, with the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Bina</i>. This limiting dynamic in <i>Bina</i> is explained further in the following sections. </i> <b>The</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that was intermingled with each and every</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>became the left side of the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i><b>, while the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>itself is considered the right side in the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i><b>, with the left side impairing the right side.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> explains, the two sides are in a conflict for dominance. Recall that in Kabbalistic thought, positional language is not literal. Thus, “right” refers to the spiritual dynamic of giving, expressed by a column of the light of giving (the light of <i>ḥassadim</i>). “Left” refers to a context that lacks the light of giving, reflected here by <i>Malkhut</i>, which only draws the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, the column of light on the “left.” The conceptual conflict operating here can be thought of as a contest between the two kinds of light. The light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> is drawn from the Creator, serving as the animating lifeforce of the created beings. These attributes indicate a certain superiority to this light. However, the light of giving (<i>ḥassadim</i>) reflects the desire of the created beings to “give back” to the Creator, reflecting their capacity for giving, and thus, attaching themselves to the Creator through an equating of form. Accordingly, one of these lights (<i>Ḥokhma</i>) pertains more to receiving, while the other (<i>ḥassadim</i>) pertains more to giving. The rectification of lines is the process by which these lines can become incorporated together, allowing the receiving to be one of “receiving in order to give.” </i> <b>Then the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>engaged in a</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of judgments of this</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> that ascended to <i>Bina</i>, <b>and the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of giving</b> (<i>ḥassadim</i>) <b>that emerged through this</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of that</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>became a middle line that unites and equates the two lines with one another. Were it not for the judgments in</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, there would be no</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, and the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>would not be plentiful.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Since the only light of this level is the light of giving, when the supernal light interacts with the partition in the fusion through collision here, it leads to the rise of a column (the middle line) of returning light of the light of giving. This excess giving, deriving from the vessel of <i>Malkhut</i>, is described by the author of the <i>Sulam</i> as an excess of the light of giving within the level. This excess reflects the activation of <i>Malkhut</i> within the level so that it is now considered equal to the right side (In <i>Talmud Eser Sefirot</i>, Vol. 7, section 56, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> provides an alternative explanation for this rectification). Because this level is only the level of the first three <i>sefirot</i> of the larger level, it only requires the light of giving (as it is a third level, a level of <i>Bina</i> out of the five overall levels), and so this rectification of <i>Malkhut</i> is sufficient. As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> proceeds to explain, the lower six <i>sefirot</i> (the six extremities) will need the illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and therefore, the rectification process for that lower level will need to be more extensive. </i> <b>Consequently, the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which is the left</b> side, <b>became as important as the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>itself, which is the right</b> side<b>.</b>
<b>It is known that the beginning of the rectification</b> that takes place by way <b>of the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>occurs in the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, which emerged after the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>. Accordingly, the rectification of the three lines also begins from the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>since one is dependent on the other. This is not the case for the first three</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i><b>,</b> <i><b>galgalta</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ab</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>, which preceded the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>. The ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>had not yet transpired in them, and therefore they did not contain three lines but just one line.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">The ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> that takes place in the second constriction only begins in the world of <i>Nekudim</i>. Since this ascent is the cause of the three “lines” or columns of light in the rectification of lines, the worlds preceding this ascent only have one column of light within them.</i>

Chapter 26

26. <b>This</b> kind of rectification <b>is possible only in the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <b>world of <i>Nekudim</i></b><b>.</b> These first three <i>sefirot</i> <b>are the first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, since the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>within them is</b> the light of <b>the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> of the level. <b>The</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>is their very essence, because they never receive the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>(as explained in the Introduction to the <i>Zohar</i>, in the <i>Sulam </i>, s.v. “<i>vehu mita’am</i>”).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">The world of <i>Nekudim</i> is from the level of <i>Sag</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> which is <i>Adam Kadmon</i>'s third level and <i>partzuf</i>. The third level in the structures of the <i>sefirot</i> and <i>partzufim</i> is the level of <i>Bina</i>, which contains the light of giving. Recall that each level (like the level of <i>Bina</i> discussed here) is also composed of five levels (the five main <i>sefirot</i>). The point in this section is that the first three <i>sefirot</i> of the level of <i>Bina</i> (the level of <i>Sag</i> and by extension, the world of <i>Nekudim</i>) contain the light of giving. The lower six <i>sefirot</i>, in contrast, require the illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and thus, a more complex rectification, as this section and those following explain. </i> <b>Therefore, the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>that emerged from upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is sufficient to unite the two lines, right and left, with each other and to return the first three</b> lights <b>to the</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>. This is not the case with the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>world of <i>Nekudim</i></b><b>, which are</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, whose essence is giving illuminated by</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Talmud Eser Sefirot</b></i> <b>1:1:50), illustrating that</b> the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> <b>require</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. Since</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is intermingled with all the</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, they cannot receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">The presence of <i>Malkhut</i> in each of the <i>sefirot</i>, resulting from the second constriction, means that the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> cannot be received by these <i>sefirot</i> below the diaphragm. The first constriction which took place within <i>Malkhut</i> means that the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> is rejected by <i>Malkhut</i>, and these lower six <i>sefirot</i> that are now intermingled with <i>Malkhut</i> because of the second constriction, reject the light as well.</i> <b>and therefore they are in a state of lack and impairment as long as</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>does not illuminate them.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Unlike the level of <i>Bina</i> in a given level, which does not draw the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, but only the light of giving (<i>ḥassadim</i>), the lower seven <i>sefirot</i> do draw <i>Ḥokhma</i> and are considered impaired as long as they are unable to do so. The presence of <i>Malkhut</i> intermingling with these lower <i>sefirot</i> means they cannot draw the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i>
<b>Consequently, the</b> <b>height</b> of the light <b>of giving</b> <b>that emerged from upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is not at all effective for them in equating the two lines, right and left, with each other. The judgments in the left, which are the judgments of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that ascended to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, impair the right and distance the light of the first three from it. Thus, the rectification of the lines of the first three is not at all effective in rectifying the two lines, right and left, that are in the</b> <b>six extremities</b><b>, since the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>in all the</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>are from the incorporation of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>there, and as long as</b> the level of the six extremities <b>does not have the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>it is in a state of lack and impairment.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">The rectification described in section 25 only applies to the higher aspect of the level, known as the “first three.” The “first three” is a general term loosely describing the higher aspect of a level by referencing the three upper <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Bina</i>. The point here is that the higher aspect of the level was broken apart by the second constriction and ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> but was then rectified through the fusion through collision and middle column described in section 25. This same process cannot work for the lower <i>sefirot</i> of the level, the six extremities. As explained in the following paragraphs, the “first three” are composed of the light of giving, while the lower <i>sefirot</i> require the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. As a result, a different method is employed to allow the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to ultimately be received by <i>Malkhut</i> in the lower levels. </i>

Chapter 27

<b>The Rectification of Lines in the Seven Lower Ones and in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <br>27. <b>Therefore, the first rectification required for the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>is to initially bring down the judgments in the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that mingled with the</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, that is, simply to extend illumination from</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> and <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, which brings down the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>and returns it to its place (as stated in section 18 above).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">The yearning of the lower <i>sefirot</i> for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> triggers the process of rectification that ultimately leads to their receiving the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. The yearning from below activates the levels of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Bina</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, which shine their light down into the levels that are constricted by the second constriction. This illumination, in a series of stages described further in later sections, removes <i>Malkhut</i> from <i>Bina</i> and returns it to its place. This allows the <i>sefirot</i> that were dislocated to the lower levels to return to their original place. Because of their relationship with that lower level, however, they retain a certain distance from their original level, represented by them operating now as the “left side” of the level.</i> <b>Then the three vessels of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>return to the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>and become the left line, while</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which remained</b> there<b>, become the right line. Since the</b> <b>level</b> <b>has been made whole</b> by having <b>the five vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, all five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, return to it (as explained there), and the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>returns to the</b> <b>level</b><b>. The middle line can then unite the two lines with each other and complete the</b> <b>level</b> <b>with all its rectifications.</b>

Chapter 28

28. <b>The second rectification is to strengthen the diaphragm (mentioned in section 16 above), which is the arresting force of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that ascended to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, in such a manner that it will never be negated. Even when the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>descends from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, its arresting force remains in the place of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. The</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that are</b> returning to <b>connect with the</b> <b>level</b> <b>must rise above the diaphragm, where they reconnect with the</b> <b>level</b><b>. However, when they are situated below, under the diaphragm, they cannot connect with the</b> <b>level</b><b>, even though the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>has already descended from there, since its arresting force remains even after its descent from there.</b>

Chapter 29

29. <b>When</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>rise above the diaphragm and reconnect with the</b> <b>level</b><b>, they do not become a single, seamless</b> <b>level</b> <b>with the two vessels of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. There remains a gap between the two vessels of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which were never impaired since they did not leave their</b> <b>level</b><b>, and the three vessels of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which left their</b> <b>level</b> <b>and were impaired at the time of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and have now returned. This gap renders them into two lines, right and left.</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>become the right line, while</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>become the left line (as explained</b> in the <i>Sulam </i>'s commentary on <b><i>Vayak’hel</i>, section 130, s.v. “<i>vezeh</i>”). </b>

Chapter 30

30. <b>This gap, and this right and left, do not refer to a location, God forbid, as that which is spiritual is beyond place and transcends time. Rather, “gap” means that they do not want to connect with each other. “Right” refers to the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>and “left” means the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>The idea</b> conveyed here <b>is that</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b><b>, which remain</b> in the level <b>at the time of</b> <b>immaturity</b><sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">The time of immaturity is a reference to the state of the <i>sefirot</i> resulting from the second constriction, before any rectifications, when <i>Malkhut</i> is partnered with <i>Bina</i>.</i> <b>with the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>, are satisfied with this</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>at the time of</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>as well, that is, also after the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>has descended from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, because this light was not impaired, as stated above.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">The light of giving is not impaired or impacted by the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i>. <i>Malkhut</i> is the essence of the will to receive, the vessel meant to receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. After the first constriction, the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> could no longer be received by the vessel of <i>Malkhut</i>, so <i>Malkhut</i> is considered “dark.” Thus, when <i>Malkhut</i> ascends to <i>Bina</i>, it stops the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from manifesting in the level. It has no impact on the light of giving, however, because the first constriction was only for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. Accordingly, the light of giving was not impaired by the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <b>They do not wish to receive the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">These <i>sefirot</i>, operating in the level of <i>Sag</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, are the essence of the level of <i>Bina</i> (which is synonymous with <i>Sag</i>, the <i>Bina</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>). <i>Bina</i> does not yearn for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, as it is the essence of the light of giving. Therefore, these vessels, unaffected by the second constriction, since they did not descend beneath the diaphragm, are not “interested” in the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. They form the right line, the column of the light of giving. As the section explains, the <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i>, now possessing some of the qualities of the level below with which they interacted during the second constriction (the phase of immaturity), remain divided by the diaphragm and now operate as the left side.</i> <b>and the first three</b> lights of <i>neshama</i>, <i>ḥaya</i>, and <i>yeḥida</i>, <b>which just returned to the</b> <b>level</b><b>, along with the return of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>(as stated in section 18 above). Therefore, the</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>are considered the right line, the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>.</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which upon their return to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>brought the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and the</b> <b>first three</b> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b><b>, do not want to connect with</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. This is because</b> <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i> <b>hold on to the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>, which they had at the time of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, whereas</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>have higher regard for the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which just arrived in the</b> <b>level</b><b>. They are therefore considered the left line because they hold on to the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 31

31. <b>This gap between the right line and the left line is also considered a dispute between the right and the left (as explained in <i>Bereshit</i> I, page 57, s.v. “<i>vezeh</i>”; <i>Idra Rabba</i> 214). The right line, which holds on to the</b> light of <b>giving</b><b>, wants to negate the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left line and to give control solely to the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>, while the left line, which holds on to the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, wants to negate the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>in the right line and to give control to the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">The conceptual conflict operating here can be thought of as a contest between the two kinds of light. The light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> is the essence of the Creator, serving as the animating lifeforce of the created beings. These attributes indicate a certain superiority to this light. However, the light of giving (<i>ḥassadim</i>) reflects the desire of the created beings to “give back” to the Creator, reflecting His capacity for giving. Thus, the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> represents the receiving of life force by the created being, while the light of giving represents the desire of the created being to emulate the Creator and reciprocate toward Him. These opposing dynamics require the mediating dynamic of the middle line to unite the two sides into a synergy.</i> <b>On account of this dispute, neither of them illuminate. The</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>in the right line lacks the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and is like a body without a head,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">The lack of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> represents a lack of animating lifeforce from the Creator, which is the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. Conversely, the lack of the light of giving means that the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> cannot be received by <i>Malkhut</i>, because of the first constriction, leaving the vessel dark.</i> <b>while the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left line is entirely dark, as the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>cannot illuminate without</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>(as explained in <i>Bereshit</i> I, page 47, s.v. “<i>nafak</i>”).</b>

Chapter 32

32. <b>The only remedy for this dispute is by means of the middle line, which is formed by the lower one ascending there as</b> <b>feminine waters</b><b>, in the mystical meaning of the middle line.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">The “lower one” refers here to the level underneath the upper level in which the second constriction transpired. Recall that when <i>Malkhut</i> ascended to <i>Bina</i>, it caused <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of that level to be blocked from that level and descend to the level below. In the phase of maturity, these <i>sefirot</i> return to their place (though there is still a division between them and the remaining <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Keter</i>, because of the diaphragm, as explained above). In addition to the return of these descended <i>sefirot</i> to their place, the <i>sefirot</i> of the lower level also desire to ascend to the upper level. As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> explains, this is because these lower <i>sefirot</i>, through their interaction with the descended upper <i>sefirot</i>, develop an affinity for that original higher level. Their yearning to receive from that level is the concept of the ascent of “feminine waters.”</i> <b>A fusing from the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>occurs on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the lower one, which is called the partition of <i>ḥirik</i>, and the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>emerges from upon it, which is the mystical meaning of the middle line.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Because this rectification, and the subsequent illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, is achieved through the vessels of the level below, this vessel is symbolized by the <i>ḥirik</i> vowel, a dot that floats below the letter, and which represents the partition of the vessel of <i>Malkhut</i> from below. </i> <b>On the one hand, this</b> <b>partition</b> <b>diminishes the first three of the left line, and on the other hand it increases the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">The excess light of giving generated by this column reduces the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from a full column to a column of six extremities. As the author of the <i>Sulam</i> explains, this allows the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to be enclothed in the light of giving so that the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> can then be received by <i>Malkhut</i> and the lower levels (including our world). </i> <b>In both regards, it compels the left line to unite with the right line.</b>
<b>Thus, the light of the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left line is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>of the right line, which it can now illuminate, and</b> thus <b>the left line is complete. Likewise, the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>in the right line unites with the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left line and thereby attains the light of the first three, and the right line is complete.</b>
<b>Consequently, it can be seen how the middle line completes the two lines, right and left. The rectification of the three lines, which transpired in the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, has hereby been explained in broad outline.</b>

Chapter 33

<b>The Emergence of Three Lines in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <br>33. <b>The order of the emergence of three lines in one</b> <b>level</b><b>, which can be applied to all the</b> <b>levels</b> <b>will now be explained in detail.</b> Let us take <b>the example of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which is the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. The first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>were re-formed as the</b> <i>partzufim</i> of <b><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma Ila'in</i></b><b>, while the seven lower ones of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>were reformed as</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">The “re-forming” mentioned here refers to the formation of the <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> that took place after a process called “the breaking of the vessels.” The <i>partzuf</i> structure of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> possess four parts, two male and two female. The upper part is <i>Abba</i> (Father, the male aspect) and <i>Imma</i> (Mother, the female aspect), while the lower part is <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, also male and female (recall that “male” and “female” in Kabbalistic writings refers to “giver” and “receiver,” primarily). The author of <i>Sulam</i> is using the lower set of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> as an example illustrating the rectification of lines, as he proceeds to explain.</i>
<b>Now there first emerged the right line of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. This</b> line <b>was formed when the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>ascended to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. This caused the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>to terminate under</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, causing</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>to fall below to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 21 above). The two vessels of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which remained in the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, became the right line, as stated above. Since there are only two vessels there,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, they contain only the two lights of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, while the first three are lacking (as stated in section 26 above).</b>

Chapter 34

34. <b>Subsequently, the left line emerged, which is</b> comprised of <b>the three vessels of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>after they returned and ascended from their fall. This</b> return <b>was established by means of the illumination from</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, which removed the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>from the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and returned it to its place, at which point</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>returned and ascended to their</b> <b>level</b> <b>(as stated above in section 21). Since</b> the presence of all <b>five vessels in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>is</b> thus <b>complete,</b> the lights of <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>are all</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in them, and then</b> <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> <b>become the left line of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>(as stated above in section 29).</b>
<b>With the emergence of the left line, a conflict arises between the right and the left: The right wants to negate the left and rule alone, and likewise the left wants to negate the right and rule alone (as stated above in section 31). Consequently, neither of them can illuminate as long as the middle line, which unites them, has not been manifested.</b>

Chapter 35

35. <b>Subsequently, the middle line emerged, and it emerged by means of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>beneath</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which ascended as</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>(as stated above in section 32). This is</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which ascended to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>together with the three vessels of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>when they returned and ascended to their</b> <b>level</b> <b>(as stated above in section 21). The type of light that emerges from upon this</b> <b>partition</b> <b>unites the right and left lines in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>into one, only that the right will illuminate from above to below, while the left will illuminate from below to above. Then the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the garment of the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>and can illuminate, and the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>is incorporated in the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and the first three are completed.</b>
<b>Consequently, before the formation of the middle line, the right line and the left line were in conflict with one another, and they wished to negate each other. The right line, as the root of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>and unimpaired</b> by the earlier ascent of <i>Malkhut</i>, <b>wants to negate the dominion of the left and subjugate it, akin to the relationship between a root and its branch. As for the left line, since it contains the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which is greater than the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>in the right line (as stated above in section 30), it therefore has greater strength to negate the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>in the right line. As a result, neither of them can illuminate, since</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is unable to illuminate without the garment of the</b> light of <b>giving</b><b>, and without the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>constitutes</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>without a</b> <b>head</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">When the light of giving appears without the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, it is considered six extremities without a head. When this lack of a head is repaired, as in this context, the entire structure is described as attaining the “first three,” referring to the head of the structure. The light of giving represents the yearning of the created being to emulate the Creator through an equating of form, trying to give. Without the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, however, the created being lacks the animating lifeforce of the Creator and is incomplete. This same perspective can be applied to the structure of these <i>partzufim</i>. Without the “first three” properly manifest within it, the <i>partzuf</i> is incomplete, and cannot function as a transmitter of the supernal light to subsequent levels.</i>

Chapter 36

36. <b>The reason that</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is unable to illuminate without the</b> <b>light of giving</b> <b>is that we are dealing with</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which comprises the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which are</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. The</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are not considered</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>itself, but rather they are</b> formed <b>from the incorporation of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, for all ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>are incorporated in one another, and each</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>contains ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>. For example, the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>is comprised of all ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>:</b><sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">The author of <i>Sulam</i> consistently refers to the ten <i>sefirot</i> as the five main <i>sefirot</i>, though within this structure of five, the full ten are present.</i> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. The</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <i>sefira</i> <b>within it is considered itself, and the</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>within it are from the</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that were incorporated inside it, while the</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which are its</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, are from the incorporation of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <b>Nukba</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Recall that each of the <i>sefirot</i> contains all the <i>sefirot</i> within it, as the author of <i>Sulam</i> reviews here. The level of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> is the lower seven <i>sefirot</i> of the total <i>Bina</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> (with <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma Ila'in</i> as the upper three <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>). The lower seven <i>sefirot</i> of any given level are meant to hold the light of giving with an illumination from the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, as this section explains. </i>
<b>It is known that the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, from its source in the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light, is primarily the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>, only that the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>illuminates its</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Talmud Eser HaSefirot</b></i> <b>vol. 1, 1:50). Therefore, it is impossible, in all the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, for</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to illuminate without the</b> light of <b>giving</b><b>, as</b> the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> would then <b>lack their main core and</b> the necessary element <b>for bearing the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, that is, the</b> light of <b>giving</b><b>. The</b> light of giving <b>is the main core of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the direct light, which is the root of all seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>that are incorporated in all the</b> <b>level</b><b>s.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">The structures of <i>partzufim</i> under discussion involve the dynamics of returning light interacting with direct supernal light. All forms of light are contained in sets of <i>sefirot</i>, the five <i>sefirot</i> (also referred to as “ten”) mentioned here. The structures of the <i>sefirot</i> containing the direct light serve as templates for all structures of <i>sefirot</i> at every level of existence. Hence, the level of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, synonymous with the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, always must have the light of giving as its core, with an illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i> <b>From here the rule that</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>can illuminate only the light of the first three</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>without</b> the light of <b>giving</b> can be derived<b>. By contrast, in the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, which are considered</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>in any of their contexts,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>cannot illuminate without the</b> light of <b>giving</b><b>, since the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>is the core of their essence. Consequently, if</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>lacks</b> the light of <b>giving</b> in the seven lower <i>sefirot</i><b>, it is darkness and not light.</b>

Chapter 37

37. <b>However, on account of the importance of the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that the left line is holding, the left line will under no circumstances submit in order to unite with the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>in the right line. What is more,</b> the left line <b>battles</b> with the right line <b>and wants to negate it, as stated. It will not submit to the right except by means of two forces that arise from the middle line, which act</b> upon the left line <b>and subjugate it:</b>
<b>a.</b> One force is <b>the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>in the middle line, which is</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>.This</b> <b>partition</b> <b>reduces the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left line from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the first three of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to the</b> lower <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <b>six extremities</b><i> <b></b></i><b>of <i></i></b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. This is so that the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>will not spread in order to illuminate from above to below but will illuminate from below to above, since this illumination is considered only</b> <b>six extremities</b><i> <b></b></i><b>of <i></i></b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>b.</b> The other force is <b>the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>, which occurs upon this</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, drawing a</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>.</b>
<b>Subsequently, since on the one hand the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left line reduced to</b> <b>six extremities</b><i> <b></b></i><b>of <i></i></b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>as a result of the force of the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, and on the other hand the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>increased against the left line from two sides – from the side of the right line, and from the side of the fusion of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the middle line – the left line submits and unites with the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>in the right line and in the middle line (see <i>Zohar</i>, <i>Emor</i> 197, in the <i>Sulam </i>). However, so long as the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>in the middle line does not reduce the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the first three of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, there is no power in the world that could unite it with the right line (see <i>Bereshit</i> 1:60, s.v. “<i>maḥloket</i>”).</b>

Chapter 38

38. <b>It is important understand that two forces operate in this</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the middle line in order to reduce the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the first three of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left line.</b>
<b>It has been explained above (section 22) that</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <b>Nukba</b><sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">This refers the <i>partzuf</i> corresponding to <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <b>on their own are unfit to receive</b> <b>brains</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">The term “brains“ can be thought of as similar to the human concept of consciousness. When a person understands more, he or she can be thought of as “more conscious.” Similarly, when there are changes in particular levels, like when a level ascends to the level above it as a result of the process of maturity, it is described as having more “brains,” meaning increased exposure to the supernal light that is accessible at those higher levels.</i> <b>because the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the attribute of judgment rules over them, and the force of the</b> first <b>constriction</b> <b>dominates</b> <i>Malkhut</i>, <b>preventing it from receiving the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. We call this</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the attribute of judgment “<i>manula</i>” </b>(lock) <b>(as explained in <i>Sulam </i>on the introduction to the <i>Zohar</i> 59, s.v. “<i>go</i>”).</b>
<b>However,</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>subsequently partnered with the attribute of mercy, meaning in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, so that due to</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>partnering with</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i> <b>are fit to receive</b> <b>brains</b><b>, namely, the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. We call this</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that partners with</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>“<i>maftaḥa</i>”</b> (key) <b>(as stated above in <i>Sulam </i>on the introduction to the <i>Zohar</i> 57, s.v. “<i>hahu</i>”).</b>
<b>Therefore, these two forces, <i>manula</i> and <i>maftaḥa</i>, are also present in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the middle line.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">After the second constriction, <i>Malkhut</i> operates in two roles. It serves as a terminating element at the bottom of a set of <i>sefirot</i> (the terminating <i>Malkhut</i>, with a partition associated with the <i>manula</i> mentioned here). It also serves as a channeling factor when it pairs with <i>Bina</i>, ultimately allowing the flow of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to reach lower levels of existence (with a partition of <i>maftaḥa</i>).</i> <b>Initially, when</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>needs to reduce the first three of the left line, it does this using the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of <i>manula</i>, which is the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the attribute of judgment, because wherever</b> this <i>Malkhut</i> <b>reveals itself, the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>flees from there (as explained in <i>Sulam </i>, <i>Vayetzei</i> 13, s.v. “<i>sitra</i>”). However, since</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>wants to compel the</b> <b>six extremities</b><i> <b></b></i><b>of <i></i></b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to remain, it subsequently conceals this</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of <i>manula</i> and operates with the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of <i>maftaḥa</i>, which is the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that partners with</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. Through its power, the illumination of the</b> <b>six extremities</b><i> <b></b></i><b>of <i></i></b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>remains (see also <i>Sulam </i>, <i>Lekh Lekha</i> 13, s.v. “<i>venitba’er</i>”).</b>
<b>It has thus been thoroughly explained how</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>ascends together with</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and how by means of its</b> <b>partition</b><b>,</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>unites and completes the two lines, right and left, that are in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, where</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>becomes a middle line. These three lines in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>are called</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> and <b>Da’at</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, as the two lines, right and left, are called</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, while</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the middle line that determines between them, is called</b> <b>Da’at</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 39

<i><b>Ḥolam</i>, <i>Shuruk</i>, <i>Ḥirik </b></i><br>39. <b>These three lines are also called by</b> the names of <b>three vowels: <i>ḥolam</i>, <i>shuruk</i>, and<i> ḥirik</i>. The right line is the mystical meaning of the<i> ḥolam </i>vowel. The left line is the mystical meaning of the<i> shuruk</i> vowel, that is, the <i>melafum</i>, which is a <i>vav</i> with a dot inside it. The middle line is the mystical meaning of the <i>ḥirik</i> vowel.</b>
<b>The explanation</b> for this <b>is as follows: The vowels allude to the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>since the</b> vowels <b>give life and movement to the letters, which are</b> like <b>the vessels. Therefore, the right line, which was established when</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>ascended to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>and lacks</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 30 above), is alluded to by the <i>ḥolam </i>vowel, which is generally positioned above the letters. This indicates that the vowel, which is</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, is not</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessels, which are the letters, but is located above the vessels.</b>
<b>The left line, which is established from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>after their return to their</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b> and <b>which hold on to the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>(as stated there), is therefore alluded to by the <i>shuruk</i> vowel, which is a <i>vav</i> with a dot inside it. This indicates that the vowel, which is</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>within the vessels, which are called letters.</b>
<b>The middle line is manifest from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below</b> and <b>rises to the higher</b> <b>level</b> <b>and balances and completes the two lines</b> of the higher level <b>(as stated in sections 32 and 35 above). If not for the middle line,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>would be unable to illuminate (as explained there). Since this rectification comes from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below, it is alluded to by the <i>ḥirik</i> vowel, which is positioned under the letters, which are the vessels, since</b> the middle line comes from <b>the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below. For this reason, we always refer to the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the middle line as the “partition of the <i>ḥirik</i>” (for more on all this, see the <i>Sulam </i>, <i>Bereshit</i> I, 9).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">Here the author of the <i>Sulam</i> refers to three different vowel symbols as analogies for the three lines. In the Hebrew language, vowel symbols tell a reader how to pronounce a particular letter. Thus, vowels are viewed in Kabbalistic thought as the animation of the letter, conveying how a vowelized letter is pronounced. This animation dynamic is associated with the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, which is the main life force of all things, in contrast to the light of giving. It is this parallelism between the vowels and the animating power of light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> that leads to the connection between the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and the vowels.<br>In the second constriction, the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Malkhut</i> ascends to the level of <i>Bina</i>, as mentioned previously. The partition that rests on <i>Malkhut</i> serves to stop the flow of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and causes the upper <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> to descend to the level below. Only <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i> remain in the level, and they form the right column of light. In this phase, the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> is blocked (as the right line is wholly the light of giving) and thus is said to be floating above them. This position is symbolically indicated with the vowel of the <i>ḥolam</i> which is a dot that rests above a letter.<br>In the next phase, when <i>Malkhut</i> descends from <i>Bina</i>, <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> are able to return to their original level. These <i>sefirot</i> now form the left column of light, and then the left side (the lower, returned <i>sefirot</i>) has the appropriate vessels for receiving the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This state of the light is reflected in the vowel called <i>shuruk</i>, which is a dot that is in the middle of the letter, symbolizing the capacity of the vessels for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.<br>However, in this state, the left side has an abundance of the attribute of judgment, stemming from the vessel of <i>Malkhut</i> stopping the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from illuminating. This brings the left side (filled with the limiting force of judgment) into conflict with the right side (filled with the unbounded force of giving). This is solved through the middle line, which mediates the left and right lines, making the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> illuminate inside the vessel. The middle line is a new level produced through the fusion through collision of the partition after it returned to its original place, at the lower end of the level. Because this light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> originates from an action that took place below the level, it is symbolized by the <i>ḥirik</i> vowel which rests below the letter.</i>

Chapter 40

<b>The Middle Line That Is above the Two Lines</b><br>40. <b>However, there is a version of the middle line that is above the two lines. This takes place in the three heads of <i>Atika</i>, with the unknown head mediating and uniting the two lines, the right and the left, which are the two heads,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Ḥokhma</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> is described as sealed because it doesn't reach the lower levels in any direct form. As the previous sections have explained, the entire process of the rectification of lines allows for the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to reach the lower created beings. However, this ultimate illumination is only a reflection of the pure light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> that is manifest at the highest reaches of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, which are below</b> the unknown head <b>(as explained in <i>Idra Zuta</i>, p. 15, s.v. “<i>veyesh peirush</i>,” and p. 27, s.v. “<i>biur</i>”).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">In this instance of the three lines, the mediating middle line is above the lower lines of right and left. The author of the <i>Sulam</i> explains elsewhere (in the <i>Idra Zuta</i>) that this highest version of the three lines, serving as the root for the rectifications taking place in the lower levels, does not have the same constrictions as the lines in the lower levels. Accordingly, the middle line here, the “unknown head,” is able to include the right and left into a unity. In the lower levels, in contrast, the partition of <i>ḥirik</i> is required, as the <i>Sulam</i> explains.</i> <b>Although these</b> three lines <b>were established to be the root of the three lines, in all three lines apart from these, the middle lines comes from below, as explained.</b>
<b>There are thus three aspects to the rectification of lines:</b>
<b>a. The rectification of lines in the three heads of <i>Atika</i>, in which the middle line is above the two lines, as stated above.</b>
<b>b. The rectification of lines in the first three,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">The first three, the upper component of each level undergoes a “milder” form of rectification of lines, since that level does not need any illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This is the meaning of the second kind of rectification mentioned here. The third kind refers to the lower half of each level, which are levels of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and the six extremities. These types of levels require the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, as explained in previous sections. </i> <b>in which there is no revelation of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>even in the left line (as stated in section 26 above).</b>
<b>c. The rectification of lines in the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, in which there is a revelation of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left line (as stated in sections 27 – 39 above).</b>

Chapter 41

<b>Three Types of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <br>41. <b>There are three types of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in</b> the world of <i><b>Atzilut</b></i>:
<b>a. The</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>direct light</b><b>, which, in the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>, is the sealed <i>Ḥokhma</i> of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Ḥokhma</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> is described as sealed because it does not reach the lower levels in any direct form. As the previous sections have explained, the entire process of the rectification of lines allows for the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to reach the lower created beings. However, this ultimate illumination is only a reflection of the pure light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> that is manifest at the highest reaches of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i>
<b>b. The first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is</b> <b><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i></b> <b>in the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>and which is called the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the right.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Recall that the level of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> was ejected from its proper place because of the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> in the second constriction (as explained in section 26 above). <i>Bina</i> itself has a higher aspect (its “first three”) and a lower aspect (<i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>). The aspect of the first three (<i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma Ila'in</i>, literally, “supernal father” and mother”) is said to be the <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the right. This is because this <i>Bina</i> is part of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, which is the <i>Ḥokhma</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i>
<b>c. The lower seven of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>in the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>and which is called the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">The illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> that is found in the lower aspect of <i>Bina</i> (<i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> is called the <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the left and represents the left line referred to in previous sections. </i>

Chapter 42

42. <b>You already know that</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>is the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, and</b> <b><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i></b> <b>are the first three of the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, while</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>are the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">See footnotes for previous two sections.</i>
<b>It is also known that there are only two</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>:</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which are called <i>Kitra</i> and the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">Normally, the head of a <i>partzuf</i> has a full set of five <i>sefirot</i>. In <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, the head area only has two: <i>Keter</i> (here called <i>Kitra</i>) and <i>Ḥokhma</i>. As this paragraph reviews, <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the head were ejected and now are part of the <i>partzuf</i> below the head's level of <i>Malkhut</i>, on the level of the body.</i> <b>The</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> <b>emerged from its</b> <b>head</b> <b>and became a</b> <b>body</b> <b>without a</b> <b>head</b>.<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> is described here as a body without a head because it is cut off from the head, thereby losing the lights of the head and remaining a body. </i> <b>That is, due to the terminating</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that ascended and arrested the</b> <b>head</b> <b>under its</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i>, <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> <b>are already situated below the terminating</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>(as stated in section 33 above) and therefore became a</b> <b>body</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">The terminating <i>Malkhut</i> refers to the blocking power of <i>Malkhut</i> that was inserted into the level of <i>Bina</i> in the second constriction, “terminating” the head of the <i>partzuf</i> at that point and relegating <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the head to the lower level of the body, with the lower <i>sefirot</i> of the body. Anything below this <i>Malkhut</i> is considered part of the body of the <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>This</b> set of <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> that were ejected from <i>Arikh Anpin</i> <b>are all referred to</b> by the name of <b>their highest</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. Since</b> this <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> <b>emerged from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>to become a</b> <b>body</b> <b>without a</b> <b>head</b><b>, it is no longer fit to receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>until it returns to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Bina</i> of the head is blocked off from the <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the head since it is now under the <i>Malkhut</i> of the head and part of the body of the <i>partzuf</i>. As a result, the sealed <i>Ḥokhma</i> embedded in the head of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> is inaccessible to it and to the lower levels.</i>

Chapter 43

43. <b>This</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> <b>is divided into two</b> <b>level</b><b>s, the first three and the lower seven. The reason for this</b> division <b>is because the impairment resulting from the lack of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which occurred within</b> this <i>Bina</i> <b>when it emerged from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, does not touch the first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>at all, since they are always in the</b> state alluded to by the <b>mystical meaning of the verse “For He delights in mercy.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:18. As mentioned in the previous footnotes above, and as this section goes on to explain, the first three of <i>Bina</i> do not need the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and only contain the light of giving (the “mercy” referred to in the verse). Therefore, the first three are not lacking anything when they are ejected from the head of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, despite now being cut off from the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> of that head.</i> <b>This is because</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>desires only the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>, not the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. Even when</b> <i>Bina</i> <b>was in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, its first three</b><sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">See the footnotes in the previous two sections above.</i> <b>would not receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, but only</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>. This</b> light of giving <b>was drawn to</b> this <i>Bina</i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>direct light</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The direct light is the first illumination from the Creator and is composed of ten <i>sefirot</i> that are the root of all creation. As a result, the characteristics of direct light and its vessels are paralleled by the characteristics of returning light and its vessels. Thus, the vessel of <i>Bina</i> in the flow of direct light is characterized by the light of giving within it, as this vessel or level within the direct light represents the power of created beings to give back to the Creator. This light of giving is drawn from the direct light to the <i>Bina</i> in our discussion here, a vessel that “yearns” for this light of giving. </i> <b>whose whole essence is</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>without</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>(as explained in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 5).</b>
<b>Therefore, the first three</b><sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">See the footnotes in section 41 above.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are not impaired at all on account of their emergence from the</b> <b>head</b><b>, and they are considered to have retained their actual perfection, as when they were in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>. Consequently, the first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>separate into a</b> <b>level</b> <b>of their own, and from them the</b> <b><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma Ila'in</i></b> <b>were established, which</b> <b>enclothe</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>downward, and which are always considered the first three,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">The point here is that although this aspect of <i>Bina</i> was ejected from the head, the area of the “first three” of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, it does not lose its status as a set of “first three” overall, because it was undamaged by the loss of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> resulting from its change in position. This is because the first three of <i>Bina</i> only crave the light of giving, which these first three can still receive while situated in the body of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>.</i> <b>even though they are situated beneath the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>However, regarding the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which are not the essence of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>but rather come from the incorporation of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>and<i></i></b><i> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i> together represent the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> in a <i>partzuf</i> structure. Recall that every individual <i>sefira</i> (such as <i>Bina</i> here) is comprised of all ten (or five) <i>sefirot</i>. Thus, this <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> has a lower set of seven <i>sefirot</i> that are (like all sets of lower seven) in need of the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This lower set of seven is, itself, also described as a full set of <i>sefirot</i> and forms the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, the lower part of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>. </i> <b>(as stated in section 26 above), since the main essence of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is the illumination of</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in</b> the light of giving <b>(as explained in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 5),</b> the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> <b>therefore require the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in order to give to</b> the lower level of <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. Since</b> the lower seven of <i>Bina</i> <b>are unfit to receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>and <i></i></b><i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>when the</b> lower seven of <i>Bina</i> <b>emerge from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, the</b> lower seven <b>are considered impaired.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">The lower seven of <i>Bina</i>, the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, require the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This is in contrast to the first three of <i>Bina</i>, which only crave the light of giving. As a result, <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> are considered impaired as long as they are outside the head of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>.</i> <b>For this reason, the</b> lower seven <b>were separated from the complete first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>and became a separate</b> <b>level</b> <b>of their own. From them the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>was established, which</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>from the ches</b>t<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">This is a lower aspect of the <i>partzuf</i> structure.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>downward. These</b> seven lower <i>sefirot</i> <b>are considered</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>without a</b> <b>head</b><b>, until the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>returns to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, at which point they obtain the first three.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">The point here is that when these different aspects of <i>Bina</i> return to the head of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> is illuminated by the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, an illumination for which this <i>partzuf</i> “yearns,” given its position as the lower seven <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Bina</i>.</i>

Chapter 44

44. <b>You can see that the essence of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the one called the sealed <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Ḥokhma</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> is described as sealed because it doesn't reach the lower levels in any direct form. As the previous sections have explained, the entire process of the rectification of lines allows for the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to reach the lower created beings. However, this ultimate illumination is only a reflection of the pure light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> that is manifest at the highest reaches of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i> <b>This is because this original</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is sealed in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>and does not illuminate to the lower ones, which are below the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>. Moreover, <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">See footnotes in previous two sections for the explanation of this term.</i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>are the original</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, which is called “the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Mah</b></i><b>,”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">The level of “<i>Mah</i>” refers to <i>Atzilut</i> and <i>Sag</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> means its third level, which is <i>Bina</i>, which is the essence of giving, as explained in the previous sections. </i> <b>whose essence is</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>, not</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. Upon the emergence of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, only the lower seven of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>were impaired, which are</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, because they were left without the first three as a result</b> of <i>Bina</i> leaving the head. <b>They are completed only with the return of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, since then</b> <i>Bina</i> <b>receives</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>and<i></i></b><i> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. At that stage, the</b> lower seven <b>are considered</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left line, meaning that this</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is revealed only by way of three lines that emerge in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, with the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>revealed in the left line of these three lines (as stated in section 34 above).</b>
<b>However, even though the first three and the lower seven of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which are the <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> and</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, returned to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>do not receive</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>directly from the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the head of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>. This is because each</b> <b>level</b> <b>receives only from the higher</b> <b>level</b> <b>that is adjacent to it. Rather, <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> receive the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>from the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the head of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, and they give to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>.</b>

Chapter 45

45. <b>The <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> are considered the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the right, because even when they are situated below the</b> <b>head</b><b>, they are as complete as they were in the</b> <b>head</b><b>, and they are always united with the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>. Only they do not receive from it, since they are always in</b> the state of <b>the mystical meaning of “for He delights in mercy,” as stated above</b> in section 43 <b>(see also <i>Sulam </i>, <i>Tzav</i> 151, <i>Pineḥas</i> 206).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">As was explained in the sections above, <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> do not draw or receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> into themselves, as their essence is the light of giving (the “mercy” referred to in the verse).</i>
<b>It has thus been thoroughly explained that the essence of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, only it is sealed in that it does not illuminate at all beneath its</b> <b>head</b><b>. The illumination of the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that is incorporated in the <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i></b>, <b>even though they do not actually receive it, is considered the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the right. Upon their return to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>the</b> <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <b>are called the supernal</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. The reason they constitute</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, despite the fact that they do not receive it, is because their unity with</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>renders the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>in <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> into a complete first three.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">While the <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> are not considered impaired by their ejection from the head, they are considered more complete when they are in a state of transmission of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> through them to the lower level within <i>Bina</i> of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>. This state of transmission is the <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the right.</i> <b>The</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that illuminates in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>is the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left, because it illuminates only in the left line. This</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left is called “thirty-two paths of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>“ (as explained in <i>Idra Zuta</i> 73), which is the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that is revealed to the</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b>and</b> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>and to the lower</b> <b>levels</b> below <i>Atzilut</i><b>.</b>
<b>However, the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the right does not</b> actually <b>illuminate at all from the</b> light <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, but only</b> shines the light of <b>giving</b><b>, since <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> do not receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, as stated above. All the more so, the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the direct light in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>does not illuminate beneath this</b> <b>head</b><b>, and this is why it is called the sealed</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. Thus, the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is not revealed, except for that of the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left. Yet this is not actual</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>but rather</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that receives</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b>and</b> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Of the three types of <i>Ḥokhma</i> examined over the last six sections, only the <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the left continues to lower levels. The final point here is that this <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the left is not actual light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, but rather a kind of reflection of the true, sealed <i>Ḥokhma</i> reflected through the higher (<i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>) and lower (<i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>) levels of <i>Bina</i> down to <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>. </i>

Chapter 46

<b>The Three Letters of <i>Tzelem</i>: <i>Mem</i>, <i>Lamed</i>, <i>Tzaddi</i></b> <br>46. <b>The</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of</b> <b>maturity</b><sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">This section discusses the structure resulting from the rectification of lines of the previous sections. As discussed above, in order for the rectification of lines to take place, the yearning from below (the ascent of “feminine waters“) triggers a flow from above the level of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, a process which ultimately causes the descent of <i>Malkhut</i> from <i>Bina</i>, the place <i>Malkhut</i> occupied as a result of the second constriction. That constricted state split apart every level from <i>Nekudim</i> downward, pushing <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the level to the level below. This constricted state is called “the state of immaturity,” while the reverted state, in which <i>Malkhut</i> descends and the rectification of lines is completed, is the “state of maturity.” The resulting structure of the flow of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> into lower levels is referred to as the “brains of maturity.” </i> is the state <b>after the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>reverted and descended from the place of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>to its own place, and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>returned to their</b> <b>level</b><b>, and the</b> <b>level</b> <b>was completed with</b> all <b>the five vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, and with</b> all <b>the five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 18 above).</b> This state is that <b>in which the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which constitutes the mystical meaning of the <i>yod</i> that entered the <i>or</i></b> (light) <b>and turned it into <i>avir</i></b> (air), <b>reverted and left the <i>avir</i> so that the <i>avir</i> once again became <i>or</i> (as explained there).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">See section 17 above for a full description of the meaning of the <i>yod</i> entering the <i>or</i> (light) and turning it into <i>avir</i> (air).</i> <b>Three</b> <b>level</b><b>s can be discerned in these</b> <b>brains</b><b>, which are alluded to by the three letters of <i>mem</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and <b><i>tzaddi</i>, which is the mystical meaning of <i>tzelem</i></b> (image)<b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">The concept of <i>tzelem</i> will be elaborated upon in the next sections.</i>
<b>The first</b> <b>level</b> of the brains of maturity <b>is the first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that were established as</b> <i><b>Abba</b></i><b> and <i>Imma Ila’in</i></b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <i>Ila’in</i> (literally “supernal father and mother”) is the name for the <i>partzuf</i> formed out of the first three of the level of <i>Bina</i> that was ejected from the head of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> as a result of the second constriction and the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <b>since they constitute the mystical meaning of the verse “For He delights in mercy,</b>” <b>and</b> they <b>never receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">See the footnotes in the previous sections that extensively explain this point.
