The first three of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, like all <i>Bina</i> levels, do not receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> but only the light of giving (the “mercy” referred to in the verse).</i> <b>Therefore, in their case the <i>yod</i> never leaves their <i>avir</i>, for <i>avir</i> is the mystical meaning of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of <i>ruaḥ</i>, which is</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">In other words, the state of <i>avir</i> is retained for the first three of <i>Bina</i>, as they remain unchanged in terms of their relationship with the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> even after <i>Malkhut</i> descends from <i>Bina</i>. This is a height of <i>ruaḥ</i> because this light is associated with <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, a level that is primarily the light of giving, with an illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> within it. Thus, the light of <i>ruaḥ</i> can be thought of as the “air” (<i>avir</i>) environment within which the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> is enclothed.</i> <b>In the</b> <i>partzuf</i> of <b><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, this</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>is considered the actual first three, and they</b> therefore <b>have no reason to remove the <i>yod</i> from their <i>avir</i>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the previous sections, the “first three” (meaning, the first three <i>sefirot</i>) of a level of <i>Bina</i> are the light of giving, not the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This means that the removal of <i>Malkhut</i> from the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Bina</i> during the reversion of <i>Malkhut</i> has no impact on the kind of light within the first three of a level of <i>Bina</i>, since <i>Malkhut</i> only affects the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. Since these first three <i>sefirot</i> are not affected by this reversion, they are called “air” (<i>avir</i>) which symbolizes the light of giving, while “light” (<i>or</i>) symbolizes the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i> <b>They are called the <i>mem</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">The letter <i>mem</i> has the numerical equivalent of 40, and, in the word-ending form of the letter, is shaped like a closed ring. </i> <b>of <i>tzelem</i>, since this letter alludes to the fact that they contain four</b> <b>brains</b><b>:</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the right of</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>, and the left of</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">There are a number of ways to count and categorize the <i>sefirot</i>. The most well-known count is that of ten, comprising <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, <i>Bina</i>, <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i>, <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, <i>Yesod</i> and <i>Malkhut</i>. This count can be thought of as the “core” <i>sefirot</i>, the root ingredients of everything in existence. However, an alternative count of ten <i>sefirot</i> removes <i>Keter</i> and adds the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Da’at</i> after <i>Bina</i>. <i>Da’at</i> is not a true substitute for <i>Keter</i>, as it is not one of the core <i>sefirot</i>. Instead, it is a pseudo-<i>sefira</i> formed during the process of rectification of lines. During this process, and as a result of the second constriction, two columns of light are formed, one associated with the right (the light of giving), and one associated with the left (the dynamic of receiving the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>). These two columns are described as in conflict, unable to “work together” and therefore unable to serve their function of merging and transmitting supernal light to lower levels. The rectification of this conflicted state comes through a middle line or column of light that ascends from below and mediates between the two sides. The root of this middle column is <i>Da’at</i>, the pseudo-<i>sefira</i> constructed to unite the opposing sides. Because this line is a mediator between the right and left sides of giving and <i>Ḥokhma</i>, it is said to have a left and right aspect.</i> <b>Each of the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>is comprised of ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, and</b> thus <b>they are forty</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>,</b> the numerical value of the letter <i>mem</i>. The letter <i>mem</i> <b>also alludes to the closed form of the</b> <b>brains</b><b>, like the ring that is the shape of the <i>mem</i>, preventing them from receiving</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">As was explained in the previous sections, the first three of a level of <i>Bina</i> do not receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> (only the light of giving), but serve as a conduit for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to travel to the levels below. </i>

Chapter 47

47. <b>The second</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>brains</b> of maturity <b>is the seven lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that were established in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and require</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in order to transmit</b> the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b>and</b> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 43 above). Accordingly, at the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, the <i>yod</i> exits from the <i>avir</i></b> of these seven lower <i>sefirot</i><b>, and the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>returns to them in order to give to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b>and</b> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. However,</b> <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> <b>do not receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>for themselves either, since they are of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and all of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, whether the first three or the lower seven, is from the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the previous sections, <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> is <i>partzuf</i> of the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> of the level of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, which is the first <i>partzuf</i> of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>. The entire level of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, the first three mentioned in the previous section , the first level of brains of maturity, and the lower seven mentioned here, do not receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This is because <i>Bina</i> only contains the light of giving. <i>Bina</i> still serves to transmit the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to the lower levels of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>. See section 36 and subsequent sections for a more complete explanation of the relationship between <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> and <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>.</i>
<b>The whole distinction</b> between the first three and the lower seven <b>is in the lower seven, which receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in order to give to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b>and</b> </i><i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. This</b> <b>level</b> <b>is called the <i>lamed</i> of <i>tzelem</i>, since this letter alludes to the fact that</b> this level <b>contains three</b> <b>brains</b><b>:</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">See the footnotes in the previous section for an explanation of the pseudo-<i>sefira</i> of <i>Da’at</i>.</i> <b>Each of the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>is comprised of ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, and</b> thus <b>they are thirty</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>,</b> the numerical value of the letter <i>lamed</i>, <b>for the right of</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i> <b>and the left of</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">In this context, the right and left of <i>Da’at</i> are united into one, as opposed to in the first three described in the previous section . </i> <b>are here considered as one, since they are the middle line</b><sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">See the previous sections (especially 33 – 38) for a fuller description of the mechanics of the middle line.</i> <b>that unites</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 48

48. <b>The third</b> <b>level</b> <b>is</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, in which the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is revealed from the chest and below, since</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i> <b>are the place of the revelation of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">In the structure of a <i>partzuf</i>, which is described with attributes corresponding to the human body, the chest corresponds to the lower six <i>sefirot</i> associated with <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. A level of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> contains the light of giving with an illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> within it. Thus, this is the third kind of “brain,” meaning a context in which the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, the “brain” of existence, is contained in a matured vessel following the previous constrictions (the first constriction and second constriction).</i> <b>This</b> <b>level</b> <b>is called the <i>tzaddi</i> of <i>tzelem</i> on account of the nine</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">From <i>Arikh Anpin</i> and downward, the original <i>sefira</i> of <i>Malkhut</i> is missing since this original <i>Malkhut</i> belongs in the higher levels beyond the effects of the second constriction. Consequently, the light of <i>Keter</i> is also lacking in these lower levels, due to the inverse nature of vessels and lights (the loss of a lower vessel means the loss of a higher light).</i> <b>each of which is comprised of ten, which totals ninety,</b> the numerical value of the letter <i>tzaddi</i>.
<b>We have thus explained the three letters <i>mem</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and <b><i>tzaddi</i> in the three</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, and</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in the broad</b> plane of the <b>world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>. However, the same applies to the smallest of details as well, since there is no</b> <b>level</b> <b>in which these three aspects of <i>mem</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and <b><i>tzaddi</i> cannot be discerned, since there is <i>mem</i>, <i>lamed</i>,</b> and <b><i>tzaddi</i> in each of them.</b>

Chapter 49

49. <b>Nevertheless, the place of the revelation of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is not in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>but in</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">This means that although there is an illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> within <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, ultimately that is only for the purpose of transmitting that light to the <i>Nukba</i>, the level of <i>Malkhut</i>, which is the true receiving vessel for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>. As the section explains, that level of <i>Malkhut</i> is the bottom of the structure of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>, the true “destination” for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i> <b>When we say that</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is revealed from the chest</b><sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">See the previous section .</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and below, this is because from the chest of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and below is considered</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>in that</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is not revealed in the first nine</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>but only in</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. As a result of this,</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is called “lower</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>“ (as explained in the <i>Sulam </i>, <i>Bereshit</i> 1:276, s.v. “<i>ve’od kama</i>”).</b>

Chapter 50

<b>Two Aspects to the Ascent of the</b> <b>Feminine Waters</b><br>50. <b>There are two aspects to the ascent of the</b> <b>feminine waters</b><sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">The ascent of feminine waters is a term referencing the “yearning” from below for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> represented by the ascent of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> to the higher levels as the middle line. In <i>Kabbala</i> and Torah thought, the concept of female denotes the dynamic of receiving, while male denotes giving. The flow of direct light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from above to below is described as the “masculine waters.” Here the <i>Sulam</i> explains the two aspects of the “feminine waters,” the yearning from below to above. It is this “yearning” from below that triggers structural shifts above to allow the flow of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to reach the lower levels.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>:</b>
<b>First, since the first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which are the mystical meaning of</b> <i><b>Abba</b></i><b> and <i>Imma Ila’in</i></b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <i>Ila’in</i> (literally “supernal father and mother”) is the name for the <i>partzuf</i> formed out of the first three of the level of <i>Bina</i> that was ejected from the head of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> as a result of the second constriction and the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <b>always show their back in relation to</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, meaning that they do not want to receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, but rather</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>, as</b> is alluded to <b>in the mystical meaning of the verse “For He delights in mercy,” as stated above,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">See section 43 above.</i> <b>and</b> also, <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>can receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>from </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>only by means of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> (as stated in section 44 above),</b> it <b>therefore</b> follows that <b>it is impossible for</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>to receive</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>by means of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> unless</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>raises up the</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. Then <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> remove their backs from</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>passes by way of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. This awakening is drawn from the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>direct light</b><b>, which extends the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>direct light</b> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 5). Consequently, whenever</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>raises up the</b> <b>feminine waters</b><b>, A<i>bba</i> and <i>Imma</i> awaken to draw</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>(see section 83 below).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">To summarize: <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> “desires” the light of giving with an illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> within it. This “yearning” activates a flow of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from <i>Arikh Anpin</i>. It also activates <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> (with its higher aspect, <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, and its lower aspect, <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>) to “turn to face” the flow of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, in order to stop blocking it, and instead, allowing the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to pass through to <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> below. <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> plays a key role here, since it is the lower <i>sefirot</i> of the level of <i>Bina</i>, and thus, has an affinity for the light of giving illuminated by the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> (like any lower set of seven <i>sefirot</i>). </i>

Chapter 51

51. <b>The</b> purpose of the <b>second aspect of the ascent of the</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is to unite the two lines, right and left, in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>(as stated in section 35 above). When the left line of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>emerges, a conflict arises between the right and left on account of which neither of them illuminate until</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>unites them together, through the mystical meaning of the middle line, at which point they both illuminate (as explained there).</b>

Chapter 52

<b>Three Come Out of One; One Exists in Three</b><br>52. <b>It has thus been explained that the second aspect of the ascent of the</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is that it is</b> there <b>in order to unite the two lines, right and left, of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, which can illuminate only by means of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of <i>ḥirik</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">See section 39 above, and the footnotes there, for a complete explanation of this concept.</i> <b>that is in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>(see the end of section 39 above), as</b> the partition <b>completes in them the middle line, which mediates between the two lines of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. It follows that three lines emerge in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that are called</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Da’at</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">See section 46 above, and the footnote there, for an explanation of the role of Da’at in the process of the rectification of lines. </i> <b>by means of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>.</b> This is in accordance with the <b>principle that the entire amount</b> of light <b>that a lower</b> level <b>causes to illuminate in an upper</b> level <b>is merited by the lower</b> level <b>as well.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">In other words, the yearning from below triggers a change above, and this change is also reflected below, in the level of origin of the yearning.</i> <b>Therefore, since</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>caused, with its</b> <b>partition</b><b>, three lines –</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Da’at</b></i> <b>– to emerge in</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>also merits three lines of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>. This is the meaning of the statement of the <i>Zohar</i> (<i>Bereshit</i> 1:363) “Three come out of one; one exists in three.”</b>

Chapter 53

<b>The</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>Root of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>which is</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><br>53. <b>During the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>of the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> of <i>Nekudim</i><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, had six vessels:</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">See section 46 above, and the footnote there, for an explanation of <i>Da’at</i>.</i> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>(since from the perspective of the lights, in which the small ones grow first, they are called</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and the first three are missing, whereas from the perspective of the vessels, in which the upper ones grow first, they are called</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, so that the vessels of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>are missing (as explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 24), and it lacked</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of the vessels.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Section 24 of <i>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</i> states: “The answer is that there is a consistent inverse relationship between the lights and the vessels. It is the nature of the vessels that the higher vessels grow first in the <i>partzuf</i>. <i>Keter</i> grows first, followed by the vessel of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and so on, until the vessel of <i>Malkhut</i>, which grows last. Therefore, we list the vessels in the order of <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i>, and <i>Malkhut</i>, from above to below, as that is their order of growth. The lights are the reverse. In the case of the lights, the lower lights enter the <i>partzuf</i> first, because initially the <i>nefesh</i> enters, which is the light of <i>Malkhut</i>, and then the <i>ruaḥ</i>, which is the light of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>, and so on until the light of <i>yeḥida</i> enters last. Consequently, we list the lights in the order of <i>nefesh</i>, <i>ruaḥ</i>, <i>neshama</i>, <i>ḥaya</i>, and <i>yeḥida</i>, from below to above, as that is the order of their entrance, from lowest to uppermost.”</i> <b>This was due to the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to the place of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the</b> <i><b>sefira</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">As was explained in section 4 above, the five main <i>sefirot</i>, <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i>, and <i>Malkhut</i> are named <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i>, <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i> and <i>Hod</i> in a level of <i>Tiferet</i>, which is the level of a <i>partzuf</i> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. The point made here, and in the next sentences, is to describe how the second constriction operated within the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> of the world of <i>Nekudim</i>. The <i>Malkhut</i> of the <i>partzuf</i> ascended to the <i>Bina</i> of the <i>partzuf</i>, which, relative to the world of <i>Nekudim</i>, is <i>Tiferet</i> (because in a level of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Bina</i> is named <i>Tiferet</i>). This ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> split <i>Tiferet</i> into two “parts,” in which one third remained above the new position of <i>Malkhut</i>, and two thirds were ejected to the lower level, along with <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i> and <i>Yesod</i>. This is the meaning of the next sentence which states: The two-thirds of <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i>, which are called in <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> the two-thirds of <i>Tiferet</i>, and <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> (as explained there) fell from the level of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> to the level below. </i> <b>since <i>Ḥesed</i></b><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>are</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 4 above).</b> <i>Malkhut</i> ascended to <b>the upper third of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, in the place of the chest.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">In the structure of a <i>partzuf</i>, matching the structure of a human body, the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Tiferet</i> corresponds to the chest of the body. </i> <b>The two-thirds of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which are called in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>the two-thirds of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>(as explained there) fell from the</b> <b>level</b> of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below, that is, to the worlds of</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Asiya</b></i><b>, which are below</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>Therefore, only the vessels of Ḥokhma</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>remained in</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>, <b>until the point of the chest.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning: until the point of the chest, which is where <i>Malkhut</i> lies after the second constriction.</i> <b>The point of the chest is the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that terminates the</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">Now the terminating <i>Malkhut</i> has ascended to the point of the chest (the place of <i>Tiferet</i>/<i>Bina</i> due to the second constriction.</i> <b>at the place of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>and brings down</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which are called TNHY</b> (<i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i>)<b>, to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below it (as stated in section 16 above). This is the mystical meaning of why</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>during the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>are always called “<i>Va”k</i> and a point,” since the six vessels –</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>– that are within</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>are called “<i>Va”k</i>,” or <i>Vav Ketzavot</i></b> (six extremities), <b>and the point of the chest, which is the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that terminates the</b> <b>level</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>, <b>is called a point (and from the perspective of the lights, in which the small ones grow first, they are called</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>is called the “point under the</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>“).</b>

Chapter 54

54. <b>For this reason,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">As a result of the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i>, it took these vessels of <i>Beria</i>, <i>Yetzira</i>, and <i>Asiya</i> into its domain, meaning, below <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>took all the vessels in</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Asiya</b></i> <b>into its domain, because</b> <i>Malkhut</i> <b>is</b> now positioned at <b>the point of the chest. This</b> positional <b>point expelled the vessels of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>into</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Asiya</b></i><b>, and it likewise returned those vessels to the</b> <b>level</b><b>s of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>when the</b> phase of maturity <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>emerged, before</b> the vessels <b>were broken.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">The “breaking of the vessels” refers to a process that took place in the world of <i>Nekudim</i>, ultimately giving rise to the world of <i>Tikkun</i> (rectification) (rectification).</i> <b>At the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, the</b> <b>terminating <i>Malkhut</i></b> <b>again descended from the place of the chest to its place under</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of the vessels of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and then the vessels of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which had fallen to</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Asiya</b></i> <b>– these are</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the preceding section .</i> <b>– ascended back to</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>. Since</b> at that point <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>acquired completion</b><sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">These <i>sefirot</i> returned to the level, completing it.</i> <b>with the vessels of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, the first three of the lights emerged upon it (as stated in section 19 above).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the footnote in the previous section, quoting from section 24 of <i>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</i>, when there are more vessels, higher lights are able to be contained.</i>
<b>Since there is no such thing as loss in the spiritual</b> plane, <b>now too</b><sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">During the phase of maturity, although the <i>Malkhut</i> “descends” from the chest, it is not truly lost from there, since there is no real change or loss in the spiritual space.</i> <b>the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>remains in the place at the chest of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>as before. It is only its power of judgment and termination</b><sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">In other words, only this aspect of the power of <i>Malkhut</i> was lowered from the chest, allowing the vessels that had been ejected to lower levels by this terminating force to return to their proper place.</i> <b>that descended to the point of this world.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">The “point of this world” refers to the low state of being of our world, the context in which the limiting, terminating force of <i>Malkhut</i> “blocks” the divine light from being perceived. </i> <b>Therefore, those vessels of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which were under the domain</b> of <i>Malkhut</i> <b>at the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and have now returned and become connected once again to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, are also</b> still <b>connected to</b> <i>Malkhut</i> <b>at the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b> even <b>after they already became reconnected to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>as</b> its vessels of <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>and completed</b> them<b>. These</b> <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> also <b>become the nine lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> of <i>Malkhut</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">In other words, these lower <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> seemingly play two roles here. When the terminating force of <i>Malkhut</i> descends from the chest, during the phase of maturity, <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> can reascend to their proper place as the lower part of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. However, the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Malkhut</i> remains at the chest since there is no real loss in the spiritual context. Thus, the <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> now lie directly below the point of the chest, with <i>Malkhut</i>. As the section explains, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> now form nine lower <i>sefirot</i>, with the <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the chest serving as their <i>Keter</i>.</i> <b>This is because the point of the chest, which is the root of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that was present there from the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, becomes</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>. Each of the three vessels of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>divides into three thirds. The three thirds of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>become</b> the <i>sefirot</i> of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>; the three thirds of</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>become for</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> the <i>sefirot</i> of <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>; and the three thirds of</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>become</b> the <i>sefirot</i> of <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. Consequently, it turns out that these</b> vessels of <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which ascended from</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Asiya</b></i> <b>at the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>and became attached to the</b> <b>level</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>causing</b> the emergence of <b>its first three lights, also become attached to</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, and become for it nine lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the vessels and the first nine of the lights.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">Before this phase of maturity, the point of <i>Malkhut</i> that was at the chest was only one vessel (the vessel that would become <i>Keter</i> with the return of the <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>) and one light (the lowest light, and the highest vessel, following the pattern mentioned previously that the vessels “appear” from highest to lowest, while the lights enter the vessels lowest to highest). Once the phase of maturity is manifest, the remaining vessels appear (<i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> form the lower nine <i>sefirot</i> below <i>Malkhut</i> of the chest, with <i>Malkhut</i> serving as the <i>Keter</i> for the structure) and the other nine lights enter accordingly.</i>

Chapter 55

55. <b>You thus find that the root of</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Nukba</i> refers to the <i>Malkhut</i>-associated <i>partzuf</i> below <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. In this context, the idea is that the root of this <i>Malkhut</i> lies upon the chest of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, as the previous sections explained.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is the point of the chest, which is not missing from</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>even at the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, which is called “</b><i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">It is called this because this point in the <i>partzuf</i> ultimately becomes the <i>Keter</i> for the structure discussed at the end of the previous section.</i> <b>Additionally, those vessels of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which fell to</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Asiya</b></i> <b>at the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b><b>, and which return to</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>at the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, divide into two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>, to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. They serve as</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of the vessels for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and as the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">See section 46 above, and the footnote there, for a more complete explanation of <i>Da’at</i>.</i> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of the vessels for</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 56

<b>From the Chest and Below of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>Belongs to</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><br>56. <b>From this is derived the</b> following <b>principle: that from the chest and below of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, that is, the vessels of</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, are the aspect of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which is called “the separated</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>.” All nine lower</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of that</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>are constructed from these</b> vessels of <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, after they become connected to</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>at the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, as explained.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">In the previous two sections.</i>
<b>Likewise, what we said</b> previously <b>is now well understood, that at</b> the phase of <b>immaturity</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>are considered “<i>Va”k</i></b> (<i>vav ketzavot</i>, or six extremities) <b>and a point,” that is, the vessels of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i>, which are the six extremities, <b>and the point of the chest</b>, which is <i>Malkhut</i><b>.</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is missing the first three lights on account of the lack of the vessels of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">As the previous few sections explained, these vessels below their levels in the phase of immaturity, during which <i>Malkhut</i> ascended to the chest, in the second constriction.</i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is missing the first nine</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the lights due to the lack of the nine lower</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the vessels.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">See the end of section 54 above, and the footnote there, for the broader explanation of this <i>Malkhut</i> during the immaturity phase. </i>
<b>Thus, the root of the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>at</b> the phase of <b>immaturity</b> <b>and at</b> the phase of <b>maturity</b> <b>has been thoroughly explained, referring to the</b> phases of immaturity <b>and</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>in the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>. And even though the vessels of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>were broken,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">The “breaking of the vessels” refers to a process that took place in the world of <i>Nekudim</i>, ultimately giving rise to the world of <i>Tikkun</i> (rectification).</i> <b>they were nevertheless rectified again in the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>with these two phases,</b> the phases <b>of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and</b> <b>maturity</b><b>.</b> This occurred <b>in such a manner that</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>are also “<i>Va”k </i></b>(six extremities) <b>and a point” in</b> the phase of <b>immaturity</b><b>, like in the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>of the seven</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, in which</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>have fallen into</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Asiya</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">As explained at length in section 53 above.</i> <b>This point</b><sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the point in “<i>Va”k</i> and a point,” explained fully in the preceding sections. </i> <b>is the root of</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. At the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, these</b> <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> <b>return to their</b> <b>level</b> <b>in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>and complete the vessels of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and the nine lower</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the vessels to its</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, which is</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, as explained regarding the</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and</b> <b>maturity</b> <b>of the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">These <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tiferet</i>, <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> return to <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and serve to complete its vessels, rendering a full set of ten vessels. Simultaneously, these vessels also serve as the nine lower vessels for the point of <i>Malkhut</i> that rests on the chest of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. The point of this paragraph is that this process, which took place in the world of <i>Nekudim</i> (as explained in the preceding sections) also takes place in the world of <i>Atzilut</i> following the breaking of the vessels and the rectification. </i>
<b>It thus turns out that these</b> vessels of <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which are from its</b> <b>chest</b> <b>and below, are the roots of the</b> phase of <b>maturity</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>.

Chapter 57

<b>Twelve</b> <i><b>Partzufim</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <br>57. <b>Every</b> <b>level</b> <b>that contains three sets of ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><b>, that is, ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>, ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the interior,</b> and <b>ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the end (as stated in sections 5 – 6 above) is called a</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. It is categorized in accordance with its</b> head, its <b>upper aspect: If the upper aspect is</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, all thirty</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>within</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>are called</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>; if the upper aspect is</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, the</b> thirty <i>sefirot</i> <b>are all called</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and so on, along these lines. There are five</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>whose structure is measured based on the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>upon the five</b> <b>levels</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b><b>. A</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>on a</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>yields</b> a <i>partzuf</i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>. A</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b> <b>yields</b> a <i>partzuf</i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. A</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the second</b> <b>level</b> <b>yields</b> a <i>partzuf</i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. A</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>yields</b> a <i>partzuf</i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. A</b> <b>partition</b> <b>at the root</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">The root level is the level of <i>Keter</i> in the partition, yielding a height of <i>Malkhut</i> in the <i>partzuf</i> structure. See the adjacent footnote for the inverse relationship between the level of a partition and the <i>partzuf</i> height it yields.</i> <b>yields</b> a <i>partzuf</i> <b>at the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>,” section 21).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">From section 22 of <i>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</i>: Consequently, five types of fusion through collision can be discerned in the partition, corresponding to its five measures of opacity:<br>Fusion through collision against a complete partition, which is formed with all five levels of opacity, gives rise to returning light that is sufficient to enclothe all ten <i>sefirot</i> – that is, until the level of <i>Keter</i>. <br>When there is fusion through collision against a partition that lacks the opacity of the fourth level, and has only the opacity of the third level, the returning light that it raises is sufficient to enclothe the ten <i>sefirot</i> only up to the level of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and does not include <i>Keter</i>.<br>If it contains only the opacity of the second level, its returning light is smaller and is only enough to enclothe the ten <i>sefirot</i> of the supernal light up to the level of <i>Bina</i>; it lacks <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i>.<br>If it contains only the opacity of the first level, its returning light is diminished even further and is sufficient to enclothe only to the level of <i>Tiferet</i>; it lacks <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and <i>Bina</i>.<br>If it lacks even the opacity of the first level, so that only the opacity of the root level remains in it, its impact is very weak and is sufficient only to enclothe up to the level of <i>Malkhut</i> alone. It lacks the first nine <i>sefirot</i>, which are <i>Keter</i>, <i>Ḥokhma</i>, <i>Bina</i>, and the six <i>sefirot</i> encompassed in <i>Tiferet</i>. </i>

Chapter 58

58. <b>However, in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>there are twelve</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>: The four</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, which are called <i>Atik</i> and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, <i>Arikh</i> and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>; the four</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which are called</b> <i><b>Abba</b></i><b> and <i>Imma Ila’in</i></b> <b>and</b> <b>Yisrael <i>Sabba</i> and Tevuna</b><b>; and the four</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>and <i></i></b><i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, which are called the “big”</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>and <i></i></b><i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>and the “small”</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>and <i></i></b><i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">The ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> in the second constriction ultimately resulted in a situation in which each <i>partzuf</i> is now paired with a “female” <i>partzuf</i>. Thus, <i>Atik</i> and <i>Arikh</i>, <i>partzufim</i> of the level of <i>Keter</i>, are each paired with <i>Nukba</i>, a <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Malkhut</i>. Similarly, the first three of <i>Bina</i> (mentioned in the earlier sections – see sections 41 – 43 for useful background on this section) become the “male” and “female” <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <i>Ila’in</i> (the supernal father and mother). The lower seven of <i>Bina</i> become the pairing of <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>. Finally, there are two “sizes” of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and <i>Nukba</i>, for a total of four <i>partzufim</i> structures between them. The author of the <i>Sulam</i> elaborates on these structures in the following sections. </i>
<b>The reason for their division is as follows: In each and every</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>there are two types of vessels: (1) vessels that emerged in the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>through a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, and these are called “vessels of</b> <i><b>Mah</b></i><b>,” and (2) vessels that broke in the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, which are called “vessels of</b> <i><b>Ban</b></i><b>.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">The “breaking of the vessels” is a complex process that ultimately gives rise to the world of <i>tikkun</i> (rectification), which is the world of <i>Atzilut</i> and downward. As this section describes, these broken vessels, from the world of <i>Nekudim</i>, descended to a low level, then were “salvaged” and served as a pairing component for the <i>partzufim</i> structures of <i>Atzilut</i> formed through the fusion through collision against the partition.</i> <b>These are rectified and ascend from</b> <i><b>Beria</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yetzira</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Asiya</b></i> <b>and connect to the</b> <b>level</b><b>s that emerged through a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>in the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, which is called</b> <i><b>Mah</b></i><b>. The vessels of</b> <i><b>Mah</b></i> <b>are considered male, while the vessels of</b> <i><b>Ban</b></i> <b>are considered female. Consequently, there are male and female</b> components <b>in each</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> from <i>Atzilut</i> and downward<b>.</b>

Chapter 59

59. <b>In addition, each</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> of <i>Atzilut</i> and downward <b>divides into the first three and the lower seven.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">This structural divide was already mentioned in sections 41-43 above. See those sections for an example of the first three of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> and the lower seven, forming <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <i>Ila’in</i> and <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>.</i> <b>Thus, there are male and female</b> components <b>in the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, and there are male and female in the lower seven</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. Therefore, from each</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> of <i>Nekudim</i> <b>emerged four</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> of <i>Atzilut</i>. <b>The two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> of <i>Atzilut</i> <b>are called <i>Atik</i> and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, where <i>Atik</i> is</b> <i><b>Mah</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>is</b> <i><b>Ban</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">As mentioned above, <i>Atik</i>, the “first three” of the <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, represents the aspect of <i>Keter</i> that is connected to the level above. <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, the “lower seven” of <i>Keter</i>, represents the embodiment of the light of the first three in the lower level. In this way, a <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i>, like the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Keter</i>, acts as a bridge between a between two vertically adjacent levels.</i> <b>The two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the lower seven of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>are called </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, with </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>being <i></i></b><i><b>Mah</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>being</b> <i><b>Ban</b></i><b>. The two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are called</b> <i><b>Abba</b></i><b> and <i>Imma Ila’in</i></b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">See sections 41 – 43 and the footnotes there for a fuller explanation of this structure.</i> <b>The two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the lower seven of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are called</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. The two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>are called the “big”</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, and the two</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the lower seven in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>are called the “small”</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 60

60. <b>The reason we do not consider</b> there to be <b>four</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">This entire section assumes the reader's familiarity with the quoted preceding sections. The main idea here is simply to explain why there is no set of male and female <i>partzufim</i> associated with <i>Ḥokhma</i> in <i>Atzilut</i>.</i> <b>is because </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>is the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Mah</b></i><b>, but the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that is in it is blocked within its</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>in the mystical meaning of “this inside that” (as explained in <i>Idra Zuta</i>, section 37) and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>does not illuminate at all in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">This concept was explained in the preceding sections regarding the rectification of lines. In short, the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> essentially “blocked” the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from illuminating into <i>Atzilut</i>. The subsequent restructuring of the rectification of lines allowed an illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to ultimately reach <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and the levels below. Section 41 above deals directly with the issue of <i>Ḥokhma</i> in <i>Atzilut</i>, though the preceding and following sections there are also relevant.</i> <b>Rather, all the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that illuminates in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>comes from the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that returned to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>and became</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 44 above). This</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>was</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> and</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. The <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> are considered the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the right, while</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>are considered the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left (as stated in section 41 above). Accordingly, we do not consider</b> there to be <b>four</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>but rather in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is also considered</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that illuminates in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>in all the worlds.</b>

Chapter 61

<b>An Important Principle regarding Time and Place</b><br>61. It is important to <b>know, with regard to all expressions in the wisdom of <i>Kabbala</i> relating to time and place, that they do not refer to the conceptualized time and place that operate in the material</b> reality<b>. Here,</b> in discussions of <i>Kabbala</i>, <b>everything is above time and above place. Rather, every</b> occurrence of the terms <b>“before” and “after” means cause and effect. We call the cause “before” and the effect “after” because every cause precedes its effect.</b>
<b>The concepts of</b> “<b>above</b>” <b>and</b> “<b>below</b>” <b>and</b> “<b>ascent</b>” <b>and</b> “<b>descent</b>” <b>are measures of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>and purity. “Ascent” means purification, and “descent” means an increase in</b> <b>opacity</b><b>. When we say that a lower</b> <b>level</b> <b>ascends upward, this means that the lower</b> level <b>was purified and became as purified as the upper</b> <b>level</b><b>, and therefore</b> the lower level <b>became attached to</b> the upper level<b>, since the</b> <b>equating of form</b> <b>attaches spiritual entities to one another. Likewise, when we say that a lower</b> level <b>enclothes</b> <b>an upper</b> level<b>, this means that an</b> <b>equating of form</b> <b>with the external aspect of the upper</b> level <b>was developed in</b> the lower level, <b>because we call an attachment to the external aspect of the upper</b> level <b>the</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the upper</b> level<b>. You should similarly interpret all other concepts that are presented in</b> terms of <b>time or place in this manner, that is, in spiritual terms, according to the context.</b>

Chapter 62

<b>Two Differences between the</b> <i><b>Partzufim</b></i> <b>of the First Three and the</b> <i><b>Partzufim</b></i> <b>of the <i>Vav Ketzavot</i> (</b><b>Six Extremities</b><b>)</b><br>62. <b>Every</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>emanates and is born from the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>above it by means of cause and effect. This occurs in all the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>, from the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, which emerged after the</b> <b>first constriction</b> (<i>tzimtzum</i>), <b>until the end of the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> the world of <i><b>Asiya</b></i><b>. Moreover, they</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>one another; that is, every lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>enclothes</b> <b>the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of its upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. For an explanation of</b> the concept of <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, see above (section 57).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">That section defines a <i>partzuf</i> as having a head, body and end, as opposed to a <i>sefira</i> which is one unit.</i>

Chapter 63

63. <b>The</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> can be <b>divided into the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three, which are the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and into the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>six extremities</b><b>, which include the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of the lower seven</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is called</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>. These</b> latter <b>three</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>are always considered the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <b>six extremities</b><b>, and even when they receive the first three, they do not leave the aspect of</b> <b>six extremities</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">There are situations in which these <i>partzufim</i> of the six extremities become connected to a set of the first three <i>sefirot</i>, but they still retain their status as the <i>partzufim</i> of six extremities.</i> <b>This is because they lack</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>at their roots, as explained in the <i>Zohar</i>, <i>Mishpatim</i>, section 520: “The head of the king is established in</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Sulam</i> idea conveyed by this quote is that even when <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> (the “king”) is established with a head (a “first three”), it still is only of the level of <i>Ḥesed</i> and <i>Gevura</i>, the first two of the six extremities.</i>
<b>There is a difference between the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three and the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>six extremities</b><b>, both regarding their emergence and birth and with regard to their</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. This is because the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three emerge from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>that is adjacent to them. This</b> process <b>begins from the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is the first <i>partzuf</i> in the layers of existence from the Creator “down” to the lowest point of Creation. This process of descending levels of <i>partzufim</i> begins there.</i> <b>After the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i> <b>emerged,</b> including <b>both the</b> <b>head</b> <b>and the</b> <b>body</b> <b>(as explained in sections 5 – 6 above), the beating of the</b> <b>surrounding light</b> <b>on the</b> <b>inner light</b> <b>in the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>commenced.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">The surrounding light, unable to become contained within the <i>partzuf</i> beats against the barrier of the returning light containing the inner light. As this section explains, this beating pressure ultimately purifies an aspect of the partition, creating a new level of returning light and a new <i>partzuf</i> as a result.</i> <b>This means that the light that the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>had blocked from entering the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>is called</b> <b>surrounding light</b><b>, and this</b> surrounding light <b>struck against the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>in whose</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>the</b> <b>inner light</b> <b>was</b> <b>enclothed</b><b>.</b>
<b>On account of this beating of the</b> <b>surrounding light</b> <b>on the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>was purified, and its form was equated to the fusing</b> <b>partition</b> <b>that is in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">This process can be thought of as follows: when the surrounding light beats against the opacity in the partition, it incrementally renders it increasingly intangible, “purifying” it of opacity. When this is complete, the partition is now identical to the partition in the bottom of the head (the mouth), and that leads to an equating of form and merging of the two partitions.</i> <b>This</b> equating of form between the partition of the body and that of the head means <b>that the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>ascended and was incorporated in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>in the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>.</b> The lower partition joined <b>in the fusion that is</b> taking place in the head<b>, since the</b> <b>equating of form</b> <b>is regarded as a unification.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">Since the two partitions are now unified through the equating of form, the lower partition can participate in the fusion through collision transpiring in the partition of the head.</i> <b>Therefore, through the</b> lower partition’s <b>incorporation in the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>, all aspects of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>were renewed, except for the last aspect.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">The aspect that was not renewed in this example context is the level of opacity of the fourth level, the level of <i>Keter</i>. Therefore, the returning light of this partition (now a partition with only opacity of up to the third level) will only reach a height capable of enclothing <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This is because the less the opacity in a given partition, the less height the rebounding returning light can reach and enclothe.</i> <b>Then a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>from the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>transpired upon</b> the lower partition<b>, upon the amount of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>that remained in the</b> lower <b>partition</b><b>, which is the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>third</b> <b>level</b><b>, and the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>emerged from upon</b> the lower partition<b>.</b>
<b>At this stage,</b> when the enclothing returning light only reaches a height of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, it becomes recognizable that the</b> lower <b>partition</b> <b>is of another</b> <b>level</b><b>, since the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>is the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, and the structure that was generated from upon the</b> lower <b>partition</b> <b>is the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, resulting from the loss of the last</b> <b>level</b> in the partition<b>. This recognizable</b> difference <b>is considered “birth,” meaning that</b> the new <i>partzuf</i> <b>emerged from the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and became a distinct</b> new <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>that has only the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Since the emergent <i>partzuf</i> is different from the original <i>partzuf</i>, the equating of forms is essentially nullified. This difference is considered “birth” because it leads to the new <i>partzuf</i> existing as distinct from the original <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>Thus, the source of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that has been born is the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>that was purified and ascended to the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i>, <b>and the place of the emergence and birth</b> of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ḥokhma</i> <b>is from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>. (All this is explained in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 35).</b>
<b>After the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>has been born and emerged from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, it</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>only the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">Even the head of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ḥokhma</i> only reaches as high as the mouth of the head of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i>. This is because it draws its origin from the partition of the body of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i>, so it can only enclothe that body and nothing higher.</i> <b>that is, on the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>, which are</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>. This is because the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>is the root</b> of the newly emerged <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ḥokhma</i> since <b>it is born from there. It</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>only the exterior of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, because the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b> <b>is external to the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>since the</b> <b>height</b> of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i> <b>is generated from the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>of the</b> <b>fourth</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">The returning light of a different, lower height is described as covering and enclothing the “outside”“ of the previous, higher <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>This is therefore considered</b> <b>enclothing</b><b>, which means the attachment to the exterior, as stated above.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">See section 61.</i>

Chapter 64

64. <b>In accordance with the explanation of the birth of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i> <b>from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>emerged from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the exact same manner. After the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>is completed, with</b> both <b>its</b> <b>head</b> <b>and</b> <b>body</b><b>, once again a beating of the</b> <b>surrounding light</b> <b>and the</b> <b>inner light</b> <b>commences, which purifies the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>and</b> creates an <b>equating of form</b> of the lower partition with <b>the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> of the <i>partzuf</i> of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. Since</b> the purified lower partition <b>is thus incorporated in the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of</b> the partition <b>of the head, the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>it contains is renewed, except for the last</b> <b>level</b><b>, which was lost.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">As in the previous example.</i> <b>The ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>thus emerge from upon the amount of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>that remains within</b> the lower partition, <b>which</b> now <b>constitutes the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the second</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">This phrase refers to an amount of opacity capable of creating a height of returning light able to enclothe as high as the height of <i>Tiferet</i>, the next in line in the series of <i>partzufim</i> under discussion.</i> <b>Since this</b> new <i>partzuf</i> <b>is recognizable as</b> being <b>a shorter</b> <b>height</b> <b>than that of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> the new <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Bina</i> <b>is considered to have separated from</b> the <i>partzuf</i> of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and is born as a domain of its own.</b> However, <b>it only</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i>, <b>since its root originates from there, as stated above.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">As seen in the previous example in the preceding section .</i> This lower <i>partzuf</i><b>, too,</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>, which is the place of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 65

65. <b>In this exact same manner, the three</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>emerged, which are</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">This section describes the process of the “birthing” of the <i>partzufim</i> of the six extremities, contrasting them to the previous examples of <i>partzufim</i> of the first three.</i> <b>However, there are two differences between them:</b>
<b>a. In these</b> <i>partzufim</i>, <b>the lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>does not emerge from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>that is adjacent to it, but rather</b> it emerges <b>from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>above its</b> adjacent <b>upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. For example,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>does not emerge from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>, but rather</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> emerges only <b>after</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>becomes one</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>with <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, which is the</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>above</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i>’s adjacent <b>upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <i>Ila’in</i> is the <i>partzuf</i> above <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, which is the <i>partzuf</i> above <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. During the rectification of lines, <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, the lower seven of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i> (discussed in sections 41-43 above) reconnects at a certain point with the upper three of <i>Bina</i> of <i>Arikh Anpin</i>, which are <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> <i>Ila’in</i>, as discussed in the previous sections.</i> <b>Similarly, the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>Nukba</i> refers to the lowest <i>partzuf</i>, corresponding to the level of <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <b>does not emerge from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, but rather it emerges only after</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>has ascended to <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">This ascent takes place in the rectification of lines described in the earlier sections of this work.</i> <b>Likewise, the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of <i>Atik</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the <i>Keter</i> level <i>partzuf</i> of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>. It is formed from the third level <i>partzuf</i> of the world of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, which is the <i>Sag</i>/<i>Bina</i> level of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, and the level from which the world of <i>Nekudim</i> originates.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>does not emerge from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the first</b> <i>partzuf</i> of <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, but from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>. The reason for this is that these</b> <b>heads</b><b>, which are considered six extremities at their roots, are unfit to fuse with the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>in such a manner that they could emanate a lower</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, and the world of <i>Nekudim</i> are all <i>partzufim</i>/levels of six extremities (the world of <i>Nekudim</i> is the six extremities level of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>). Accordingly, such a level cannot generate a new <i>partzuf</i> due to its lower positioning relative to the supernal light.</i>
<b>b. The second difference concerns the</b> <b>enclothing</b><b>. The</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>do not</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the first three of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of their upper</b> <i>partzuf</i>, <b>which is</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, but rather they</b> enclothe <b>the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i>, <b>which is</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, which are from the</b> <b>chest</b> <b>and below.</b> The reason for this is <b>that as</b> the lower <i>partzufim</i> <b>are</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>from their roots,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">Since these lower <i>partzufim</i> are <i>partzufim</i> of the six extremities, they are inherently lower, and subsequently only cover the lower portion of the body of the upper <i>partzuf</i>, that of <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i> (these three are considered the lower sefirot of the partzuf, and are thus the six extremities. The <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i>, and <i>Tiferet</i> of the upper <i>partzuf</i> is considered the “first three” here, the “upper” part of the <i>partzuf</i>).</i> <b>they cannot hold onto the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i><i> <b></b></i><b>of the <i></i></b><b>body</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i>.
<b>The two differences between the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>and the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the </b><b>six extremities</b> <b>have thus been thoroughly explained. One concerns the emergence, that only the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three emerge from the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>that is adjacently above them. This is not the case for the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>six extremities</b><b>, because they emerge from the</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>above the adjacent upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. The other concerns the</b> <b>enclothing</b><b>, that only the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three can hold on to the</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i>, <b>which are the first three</b> <i>sefirot</i> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">As described in the preceding sections, when a <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ḥokhma</i> (a <i>partzuf</i> of the first three) emerges, it enclothes the preceding <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Keter</i> from the mouth and below. This means it enclothes the “first three” of the body, the <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i>, and <i>Tiferet</i>. In contrast, the <i>partzufim</i> of six extremities can only enclothe their preceding <i>partzufim</i> from the chest and downward, meaning, the six extremities of the body, which are <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> <b>This is not the case for the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the </b><b>six extremities</b><b>, since they hold on only from the</b> <b>chest</b> <b>and below, that is, only the </b><b>six extremities</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 66

<b>Three Criteria for the Emergence of a Lower</b> <i><b>Partzuf</b></i> <br>66. <b>There are three criteria for the process of</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>for the birth of a lower</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">“Lower <i>partzuf</i> here refers to the emergent <i>partzufim</i> discussed in the preceding sections.</i>
<b>The first criterion is the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>that fuses with the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>through a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, giving rise to the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>and</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>.
