The</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the lower</b> new <i>partzuf</i> <b>will be commensurate with the measure of the</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>(as explained in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 21).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">The height of the new <i>partzuf</i> is a function of the height of returning light that the partition releases, as that returning light enclothes the previous <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>In this way, after the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>generated all the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>and the</b> <b>levels</b> <b>in the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, which did not endure but were broken and negated,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the breaking of the vessels of <i>Nekudim</i>, a complex process that is explained elsewhere.</i> <b>and the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>was purified</b><sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">This purification takes place in the process that was explained previously, in section 63 above, through the beating of the surrounding light against the inner light.</i> <b>from all its five</b> <b>level</b><b>s of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>and returned to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>(as explained in</b> <i><b>Talmud Eser Sefirot</b></i><b>, part 8, sections 2 and 4), all the</b> <b>levels</b> <b>that had emerged in</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>left their remnants in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to remnants of opacity. </i> <b>Therefore, when the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>was incorporated in the fusion in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>, those previous remnants were renewed within it.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">The renewal of these remnants gives rise to new releases of returning light to create the <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i>
<b>At first, the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>generated its highest</b> <b>level</b><b>, which constituted the remnant of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>. This is called “<i>Atik</i> of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>,” which is the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the fourth</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote">This remnant generated returning light of a height of <i>Keter</i>, forming the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Atik</i>, the <i>Keter</i> level <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i> <b>The other remnants that were in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>migrated with the birth of <i>Atik</i> to the place of <i>Atik</i>. Once <i>Atik</i> was completed, a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>was performed upon its</b> partition<b>, on the uppermost</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the remnant in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>within it, which is the third</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">This means it contained opacity up to the third level, able to generate returning light that could climb as high as a height of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i> <b>and generated the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">This is a <i>partzuf</i> of the height of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i> <b>upon it. The remaining remnants in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, which had not yet had a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>performed upon them, descended with the birth of </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>to the place of </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>. When </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>was completed, a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>was performed upon it, on the uppermost</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the remnant in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, which is the second</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote">This opacity of the second level can generate returning light of the height of <i>Bina</i>.</i> <b>producing a</b> <b>height</b> <b>of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to a <i>partzuf</i> of the first three of <i>Bina</i> as was described in sections 41 – 43 and elsewhere in the preceding sections.</i> <b>upon it, and so on in the same manner. Thus, all the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>emerge by means of a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>with the</b> <b>partition</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 67

67. <b>The second criterion is that</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of every lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>are attached to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of their upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote">This means that the upper part of a <i>partzuf</i>, the part that lies above <i>Bina</i>, where the second constriction begins its impact, are attached the <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the level above. This is the same concept of the connection between levels developed as a result of the second constriction and the rectification of lines discussed in section 20 and in subsequent sections.</i> <b>Therefore, when the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>is completed and raises its</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, the</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>also rises with them to the place of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>(all this has been explained at length in section 20 above) and are incorporated in the fusion of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. Thus, each lower one receives its</b> <b>height</b> <b>from the fusion of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper one.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">Through this ascent of a lower level <i>partzuf</i> to a higher level, the lower one is able to participate in the fusion through collision of the higher level.</i>

Chapter 68

68. <b>The third criterion is that since</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>ascends to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>and unites and completes the lights</b><sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the rectification of lines described and referred to in many of the preceding sections, from section 20 until this section.</i> <b>of the right and left of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>– and without</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>ascending as</b> <b>feminine waters</b><sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">The ascent of feminine waters is a term referring to the “yearning” from below for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> represented by the ascent of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> to the higher levels as the middle line. In <i>Kabbala</i> and Torah thought in general, the concept of female denotes the dynamic of receiving, while male denotes giving. The flow of direct light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from above to below is described as the “masculine waters.”</i> <b>the right and left of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>would be unable to illuminate</b><sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">As was explained in the extensive discussion of the rectification of lines, without a “middle line” formed by the ascent of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> as feminine waters, there would be no mediation of the right and left lines (the columns of light of giving and <i>Ḥokhma</i>, respectively). As a result, there could be no illumination from <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> to the levels below, since the right and left lines essentially negate each other.</i> <b>– it turns out that the ascent of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b> <b>has caused the emergence of three lines: the right, the left, and the middle, which are the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Da’at</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote">The emergence referred to here is that by the ascent of the middle line (<i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, which is also the pseudo-<i>sefira</i> of <i>Da’at</i> mentioned here, the three lines are able to work together, instead of negating one another. Through this complementary dynamic, they are able to illuminate to the levels below.</i>
<b>There is a rule that the total measure that a lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>causes to illuminate in an upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>is merited by the lower one as well.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote">Since the lower <i>partzuf</i> was the impetus for the change in the higher <i>partzuf</i>, the qualities that emerge in the upper <i>partzuf</i> also emerge in the lower one.</i> <b>Accordingly,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>receives the same</b> <b>brains</b><sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">See section 46 above for a more extensive explanation. The main idea is that the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, the “brains,” represents the animating divine lifeforce within all created beings. Since <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> activated greater illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> in <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i>, by serving as the middle line (the feminine waters), <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> also receives that same illumination of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i><i> <b></b></i><b>of <i></i></b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Da’at</b></i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Yisrael Sabba</b></i><b> and <i>Tevuna</i></b><b>. This is the mystical meaning of the statement “Three come out of one; one exists in three” (as explained in the <i>Zohar</i>, <i>Bereshit</i> 1, section 276, s.v. “<i>ve’od</i>,” and as explained in section 52 above). The three criteria for the process of fusion for the emergence of a lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>have</b> now <b>been explained.</b>

Chapter 69

69. <b>The main element of the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>for the emergence of the lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>is in the mystical meaning of a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>of the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>upon the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, as stated above, since this</b> determines the <b>measure</b> of <b>the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the lower</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>, as is known. However, the awakening of the</b> <b>feminine waters</b><sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote">The ascent of feminine waters is a term referencing the “yearning” from below for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> represented by the ascent of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> to the higher levels as the middle line. In <i>Kabbala</i> and Torah thought generally, the concept of female denotes the dynamic of receiving, while male denotes giving. The flow of direct light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> from above to below is described as the “masculine waters.”</i> <b>of the lower one is also required, and this awakening is performed via the</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the lower</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>that are attached to the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the upper one.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">As was explained in the discussion of the rectification of lines, and the adjoining sections (section 20 and in subsequent sections), the <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of an upper <i>partzuf</i> are ejected and join the <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the level below as a result of the second constriction. The desire for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> in <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i> of that lower level leads to a process in which the phase of maturity is initiated and <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> can return to their original, higher level. As this section explains, the <i>Keter</i> and <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the level below ascend with the <i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i> of the level above. This allows <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> to participate in the fusion through collision of the <i>partzuf</i> above <i>Yisrael Sabba</i> and <i>Tevuna</i> (as explained in section 65b).</i> <b>Consequently, both are necessary for the emergence of a lower</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>In the case of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, there is another factor</b> at work: <b>Its</b> <b>partition</b> <b>does not draw the vessels of the first three, since it is a</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote">Since the partition at the bottom of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> only has the opacity of the first level, it can only create returning light of the height of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, meaning of the six extremities, as opposed to a height tall enough to enclothe the first three <i>sefirot</i> (as explained in the preceding sections).</i> <b>and therefore the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>cannot give</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>brains</b> <b>from the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b> with <b>the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>. This is why the aforementioned third criterion is required, that</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>receive the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>by causing</b> the emergence of <b>brains</b> <b>in its upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>, constituting the mystical meaning of “three come out of one; one exists in three,” as stated above.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">See section 68.</i>

Chapter 70

<b>Three Stages in the Emergence of the Ten</b> <i><b>Sefirot</b></i> <br>70. <b>The first stage occurs in the first</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, where the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerged all at once.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">As will be explained, the concept of “stages” here refers to three different ways the <i>sefirot</i> and <i>partzufim</i> structures emerge in the structure of reality. If one thinks of existence as a tall stack, in which <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is the highest area and this world is the lowest, then it is as if there are three different “areas” in the stack. Each of these areas has different structural properties, giving rise to differences in the emergence of the <i>partzufim</i> of each area. The first area is the first three <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. The second is the world of <i>Nekudim</i>. The third is the world of <i>Atzilut</i> and downward. In the world of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> there is only one phase of emergence. In <i>Nekudim</i> there are two, and in <i>Atzilut</i> there are three.</i> <b>Upon the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the fourth</b> <b>level</b><b>, the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerged at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>. Upon the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b><b>, the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerged at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. Upon the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>on the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the second</b> <b>level</b><b>, the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerged at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">As the preceding sections explained, the partition that lies upon <i>Malkhut</i> at the bottom of the <i>sefirot</i> of the direct light creates returning light that ascends and enclothes the direct light as a new vessel. The height of that returning light is determined by the opacity within the particular partition. This opacity varies within different levels because the surrounding light beats against the partition of any given level, purifying the partition of its degrees of opacity.</i>

Chapter 71

71. <b>The second stage is the</b> <b>world of <i>Nekudim</i></b><b>, which emerged from upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote">The first three <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> emerged as a result of the direct light impacting the partition in a fusion through collision and creating returning light. The partition initially contained opacity of the fourth level, then was purified to the third level, then the second. Each level of opacity created a different height of returning light, with the fourth level creating a height of <i>Keter</i>, the third level creating one of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, and the second level creating one of <i>Bina</i>. At this point in the process, the second constriction occurred, leading to the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> in every <i>sefira</i> from that level onward. The partition in this context has opacity of the first level, since the previous levels were purified from the partition in the previous fusions through collision.</i> <b>that is attached to</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, in which ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerged at two</b> distinct <b>times.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">As this section explains, as a result of the new situation created by the second constriction, the creation of the <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Nekudim</i> requires two stages.</i>
<b>Initially the</b> <i>sefira</i> of <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>ascended to</b> the <i>partzuf</i> of <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i></b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">This is the ascent of the second constriction, beginning only at this point and downward in the structured “stack” of existence.</i> <b>Then, when the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>was purified to the first</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the purification that takes place as a result of the surrounding light beating against the vessel of the returning light after a fusion through collision has taken place.</i> <b>which is called the “apertures of the eyes,”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">The aperture of the eyes refers to the level of <i>Ḥokhma</i> of the head of the <i>partzuf</i>. </i> <b>the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>ascended and attached itself to the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, terminating the</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">This termination is the result of the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> and its partition to the higher position of <i>Bina</i>. This new placement prevents the supernal light from continuing onward and leads to a fusion through collision at that point. This is the same concept as that discussed in many previous sections regarding the rectification of lines and the descent of lower aspects of a level (<i>Bina</i>, <i>Tiferet</i> and <i>Malkhut</i>) to the level below.</i> <b>under</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, which is called “eyes.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">The five aspects of the human head correspond to five “features” of the head of a <i>partzuf</i> and, as always, to the five main <i>sefirot</i>. Those five features are the skull (<i>gulgalta</i>), eyes (corresponding to <i>Ḥokhma</i>), ears (<i>Bina</i>), nose (<i>Tiferet</i>) and mouth (<i>Malkhut</i>).</i> <b>Thus, only two vessels were left in the</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, with two lights,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">Recall that higher vessels always come in first, while lower lights always come in first. Hence, when the lower vessels are ejected, the higher lights also leave.</i> <b>while three</b> remaining <b>vessels –</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>– fell from the</b> <b>level</b><b>. This</b> state <b>is called “the</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">As was discussed previously, the phase of immaturity is when <i>Malkhut</i> remains in <i>Bina</i>, constricting the supernal light. The phase of maturity is when <i>Malkhut</i> descends back to its proper place, allowing the level to have a full set of vessels and lights once again.</i> <b>At the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, the three vessels,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, were returned to the</b> <b>level</b><b>, and the five vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, were completed in the</b> <b>level</b><b>, together with the five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>(in the manner explained in section 19 above).</b>
<b>It has thus been explained that in the</b> <b>world of <i>Nekudim</i></b> <b>the ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>did not emerge all at once, as in the first three</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>. Rather, they emerged at two</b> distinct <b>times, during the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and during the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>, with only two</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerging at the phase of</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>and the other three</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerging at the phase of</b> <b>maturity</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 72

72. <b>The third stage is the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, in which ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerged at three</b> distinct <b>times, which are called gestation, infancy, and</b> <b>brains</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">These terms are explained in the end of this section and the ensuing sections.</i> <b>Here, for the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, a purification of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>was added on the last</b> <b>level</b>.
<b>This is because the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>was purified from the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is called the “apertures of the eyes,” into a</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">There are five levels of opacity in a partition, as was referred to in the previous footnotes. The fourth level opacity is the most opaque, giving rise to a height of returning light capable of enclothing as high as <i>Keter</i>. The least amount of opacity is that of the “root” level, capable only of generating returning light of the height of <i>Malkhut</i>.</i> <b>(in the manner explained in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>,” section 21), whose</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>only the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the light of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, which is called forehead. Therefore, this light is called “</b><i><b>Mah</b></i> <b>that emerges from the forehead,” since the</b> <i>sefirot</i> of <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>are called</b> <i><b>gulgalta</b></i><b>, eyes, ears, nose, mouth. The forehead is</b> <i><b>gulgalta</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">The five aspects of the human head correspond to five “features” of the head of a <i>partzuf</i> and, as always, to the five main <i>sefirot</i>. Those five features are the skull (<i>gulgalta</i>, corresponding to <i>Keter</i>), eyes (corresponding to <i>Ḥokhma</i>), ears (<i>Bina</i>), nose (<i>Tiferet</i>) and mouth (<i>Malkhut</i>).</i>
<b>Consequently, two descents of the</b> <i>sefira</i> of <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>are required here: (a) its descent from the forehead to the apertures of the eyes, which is called “infancy,”</b> and <b>(b) its descent from the apertures of the eyes to its place, to the</b> <b>mouth</b><b>, which is called “</b><b>brains</b><b>.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">The result of these descents is a change in the related levels, allowing for the supernal light to return to the levels. This is explained further in the following sections. These newly modified conditions are termed “gestation,” “infancy” and “brains.”</i> <b>Thus, the first</b> <b>height</b> of returning light<b>, which emerges upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the previous section , this level of opacity in a partition only generates returning light of the height of <i>Malkhut</i>, the lowest height.</i> <b>is called “gestation.” The second</b> <b>height</b> of returning light<b>, which emerges upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>after the descent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, is called “infancy.” The third</b> <b>height</b> of returning light<b>, which emerges upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>after the descent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to its place, is called “</b><b>brains</b><b>.”</b>
<b>It has thus been explained that in the world of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>emerge at three times, which are called gestation, infancy, and</b> <b>brains</b><b>. The meaning of this will be explained below.</b>

Chapter 73

<b>Gestation, Infancy, and</b> <b>Brains</b> <b>of the Back and Gestation, Infancy, and</b> <b>Brains</b><i> <b></b></i><b>of the Face<i></i></b><br>73. <b>It has already been explained that the</b> <b>height</b> of returning light <b>that emerges from</b> a fusion through collision <b>upon the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>that contains only the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root is called the “</b><b>height</b> <b>of gestation,” which is the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>in the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">Since the returning light only reaches the height resulting from opacity of the root level, it can only reach as “high” as the light of <i>nefesh</i>, which is the lowest of the five lights. Since this is the only light that can be contained in such a situation, the vessel containing it is the highest vessel, the vessel of <i>Keter</i>. The reason why the vessel is the highest although the light is the lowest is because of the inverse relationship between vessels and lights discussed in earlier sections, in which the vessels appear from highest to lowest, while the lights manifest from lowest to highest.</i> <b>From the perspective of the three lines contained within it, it is called the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote">The author of the <i>Sulam</i> is explaining here that the height of <i>Malkhut</i> is often referred to as <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i>, and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> <b>However, it also contains the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">This is the next light above <i>nefesh</i>. This higher level is contained within the lower level here, which is the reason this stage is called “gestation,” as the author of the <i>Sulam</i> proceeds to explain.</i> <b>which is called the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, only it is without vessels,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">This is explained in the next section .</i> <b>and therefore the</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>must be</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the vessels of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>. Accordingly, the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of gestation is called “three within three,” meaning,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>within</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 74

74. <b>The meaning of</b> all <b>this is as follows: Although the purification of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>causes it to lose the last</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">As was mentioned previously, the partition of a given level loses “layers” of opacity after generating a column of returning light. The returning light serves as a vessel for the supernal light, but only a certain amount can be contained, called the “inner light.” The remaining supernal light, surrounding light, beats against the vessel of the returning light, eroding the opacity within it until it is purified. The “last level” referred to here is relative, meaning, the surrounding light erodes the most opaque level of the partition that is present in a given context.</i> <b>on account of which the five</b> <b>heights</b> of <i>partzufim</i> <b>are positioned one beneath the other (as explained in detail in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, sections 40–41), the last</b> <b>level</b> <b>is, nevertheless, not entirely lost. Rather, a trace of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>remains of it in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>(as explained there in section 42).</b>
<b>For example, when the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i> <b>was purified and ascended to the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">When a partition is purified of opacity, it then ascends to the head of its <i>partzuf</i> where it unites with the partition of the head. In that new context, remnants of its previous opacity are renewed (except the lowest level directly eroded by the surrounding light) and it is now able to undergo a new fusion through collision, creating a new <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>it was incorporated in the fusion there and its remnants were renewed. From the perspective of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, upon which the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>occurred, only the trace of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b> <b>remained in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, since the last</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is the fourth</b> <b>level</b><b>, was lost.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">These levels are specific to this example. In an example in which the partition had previously had the second level eroded directly, only the trace of opacity of the first level would have been renewed, while the second would have been lost.</i> <b>However, the</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>part of the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>still remained in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">This is the key idea of this paragraph. Although the lowest level of the partition is eroded and lost because of the returning light, only one of two aspects of this level are fully lost. The traces, or remnants of opacity of the level are fully lost. There remains, however, a remnant of that level of the partition called “the traces of enclothing.” This remnant, while unable to participate in a fusion through collision on its own, can join an existing fusion through collision with renewed opacity in the partition.</i>
<b>It thus turns out that there are two upper aspects that are fit for</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>: (a) the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">This is the level with the greatest opacity remaining in the partition after the erosion of the surrounding light in this particular example.</i> <b>which blocks the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>and receives the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>upon which the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>emerges,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote">This is the new <i>partzuf</i> generated in this example as a result of the third level of opacity generating returning light of the height of the level of <i>Ḥokhma</i>.</i> and <b>(b) the aspect of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the fourth</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">This is the remnant of the fourth level of opacity of the partition that was not lost, the “trace of enclothing.”</i> <b>Although</b> the aspect of enclothing <b>is unfit for a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, since it does not contain</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>that blocks the spread of light, nevertheless, when it is incorporated and participates in the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b><b>, a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>occurs upon it as well, and a</b> <b>height</b> <b>near to that of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote">Returning light that is the height of <i>Keter</i> is generated by opacity of the fourth level in a partition. Since the aspect of enclothing here is a remnant of the fourth level, the height of light generated by it in this second-hand fusion through collision is also that of <i>Keter</i>.</i> <b>is generated from it.</b>
<b>These two</b> <b>heights</b> <b>are called “male” and “female.” The</b> <b>height</b> <b>that emerged upon the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>participating with the third</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>opacity</b><b>, is called “male,” while the</b> <b>height</b> <b>that emerged only upon the third</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>opacity</b> in the partition<b>, is called “female.” (All this is explained in </b><i><b>Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</b></i><b>, section 42.)</b>
<b>Along the same lines, when the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">This is the same situation as the previous example, except that it relates to the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Ḥokhma</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> instead of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. As a result, each of the levels discussed are reduced by one, since <i>Ḥokhma</i> is the level one step down from <i>Keter</i>.</i> <b>was purified and ascended to the</b> <b>mouth</b> <b>of its</b> <b>head</b><b>, two remnants,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the remnants of opacity and the remnants of enclothing mentioned in the preceding paragraphs.</i> <b>male and female, remained in it as well, in the manner described above with regard to the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>. The trace of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b><b>, which joins the</b> <b>opacity</b> of the partition <b>of the second</b> <b>level</b><b>, generates nearly the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and this is the male aspect. The trace of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the second</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is the core element that undergoes a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, generates the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is the female aspect.</b>
<b>In the same manner, there are male and female</b> aspects <b>in the purification of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. The male</b> aspect <b>is nearly at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, while the female is at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the</b> level of the <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>for the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">The <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Nekudim</i> refers to the structure that emerges at this point in the levels of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, yielding the world of <i>Nekudim</i>.</i>
<b>Similarly, there are male and female</b> aspects <b>in the purification of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>. The male, which constitutes the trace of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>that remained in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, which joins with the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root</b> <b>level</b> in the partition<b>, is nearly at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, that is, the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. This is the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>, which is the height of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>. The female, which constitutes the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the root and which receives a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, is at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>. This is the structural height of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which is called</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>from the perspective of the three lines.</b>

Chapter 75

75. <b>We can thus discern that there are two</b> <b>heights</b> <b>of “three within three” at the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of gestation:</b><sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">Here the author of the <i>Sulam</i> returns to his original point. After explaining the male height that emerges from the traces of enclothing of the previous, lost level of opacity in the partition, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> returns to explaining the concept of gestation, in which the male aspect resulting from the height of enclothing is “within” the female aspect, the height of opacity.</i> <b>the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>. The</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>– which is the mystical meaning of the male</b> aspect <b>– emerges upon the trace of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, which joins with the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root, while the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b>and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, which is the female</b> aspect, <b>emerges solely from the trace of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root</b> level in the partition<b>. Since the trace of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>is unfit to undergo a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>unless it joins with the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root</b> <b>level</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">The example of the “root level” here is incidental to the context. The male aspect must join with whichever level of opacity currently remains in the partition in order to participate in a fusion through collision. In this context, the remaining opacity is that of the root level.</i> <b>the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>cannot stand on its own but must be</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>. Therefore, the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>gestation</b><b>, which constitutes</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>together, is considered “three within three,” that is,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>within</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 76

76. <b>Now, after the aforementioned two</b> <b>heights</b> <b>emerge –</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>within</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>– through the incorporation of</b> the partition in <b>the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>, and the</b> two heights <b>are distinguishable as new</b> <b>heights</b> <b>that differ from the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>, this distinction is considered</b> a <b>birth.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">As in the previous sections, when a particular structure is identical to another structure, the two are considered spiritually unified, through the concept of equating of form. When a distinction is discernable, they become “separated” into two distinct entities, which is considered a “birth” of the new entity.</i> <b>That is, it is recognized that a new</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>has been born here, which differs from the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. The</b> new <i>partzufim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">The plural language here refers to the two different heights that are at play in this phase of “gestation,” the “female” structure of vessels, and the male structure that is “within” the female structure and lacks vessels of its own.</i> <b>descend and</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>;</b><sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">A <i>partzuf</i> that emerges from a fusion through collision in the head of its upper <i>partzuf</i> always descends and enclothes the body of the upper <i>partzuf</i>, as described here. This new, enclothing <i>partzuf</i> has its own head and body, both of which are below the mouth of the previous, higher <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>if they are the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the first three, they</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the first three of the</b> <b>body</b><b>, which are</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and if they are the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of the </b><b>six extremities</b> <b>they</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>, which are</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, that are from the chest</b> of the <i>partzuf</i> <b>and below. They also draw the light from the upper</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, and this flow causes the descent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from the forehead to the apertures of the eyes, at which point</b> <i>Malkhut</i> <b>again receives the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>which is attached to</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, as was the case in the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">The world of <i>Nekudim</i> was built out of a fusion through collision against a partition of the first level, the level of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. When the partition descends back to this same level (from the forehead back to the apertures of the eyes), it regains the opacity of the first level.</i> <b>Then the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>also acquires the attribute of vessels,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">Since the partition now has opacity of the first level, it can generate a fusion through collision that creates vessels of the level of <i>ruaḥ</i>. This allows the “gestated” <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i> and <i>Tiferet</i> to emerge as their own height in their own vessels, instead of only within the vessels of the level of <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i> and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> <b>and they no longer require the vessels of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>. Consequently, as a result of the drawing</b> of light,<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">In Hebrew, the term for “drawing the light” here is <i>yenika</i>, “suckling,” which is also the name for the second phase (of three, gestation, infancy and brains), “infancy.” The drawing of the light leads to the formation of vessels for a height of <i>ruaḥ</i>, which is the phase of infancy. The following phase, discussed below, is the phase of “brains.”</i> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>spread out and emerge from within</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and then</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>has a complete structural height of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>.</b>
Take, <b>for example, the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of <i>Atik</i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the <i>Keter</i> level <i>partzuf</i> of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>. Initially, the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>ascended, through purification, to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>. After</b> the partition's <b>last</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the aspect of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>was lost,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Levels of opacity are “eroded” by the beating of the surrounding light against the vessels containing the inner light.</i> <b>the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the aspect of the root, called “forehead,” remained in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, with the remnant of</b> <b>enclothing</b><sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">See section 74 above for the full explanation of this term.</i> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>. Then, two</b> <b>heights</b> <b>emerged upon it,</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, “three within three,” since</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>have no vessels, as mentioned above.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">This is the phase of “gestation” in the example.</i> <b>When</b> these two heights <b>are recognized as a new</b> <b>height</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">This means that the new structure is distinguishable, which is the definition of “birth,” spiritually speaking.</i> <b>they are considered to have emerged and been born and come to their place, that is, to</b> <b>enclothe</b> <b>from the navel and below of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>. Since</b> <i>Atik</i> <b>is a</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of the </b><b>six extremities</b><b>, it</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>only the</b> <b>six extremities</b> <b>of the</b> <b>body</b><b>, as stated above, and this is called “the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of <i>Atik</i>.” Afterward, by means of</b> <i>Atik</i>'s <b>drawing</b> the light <b>from the</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>, it brings down the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>from the</b> <b>forehead</b> <b>to the apertures of the eyes, at which point vessels emerge for its</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>as well, which spread out from within</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>. The two aspects known as gestation</b><sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">As explained, this is the phase when <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i> and <i>Tiferet</i>, the structural height generated by the remnant of enclothing, are “inside” the structural height of <i>Netzaḥ</i>, <i>Hod</i> and <i>Yesod</i>, lacking their own vessels.</i> <b>and infancy</b><sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">As explained, this is the phase when, as a result of the drawing of light, the partition descends to the aperture of the eyes, regaining the opacity of the first level. This allows the partition to give rise to returning light vessels of the structural height of <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i> and <i>Tiferet</i>, allowing them to emerge from “gestation” into a full level (a level of <i>ruaḥ</i>).</i> <b>have</b> now <b>been explained.</b>

Chapter 77

77. <b>We will now explain the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>brains</b><b>. After the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>receives the two aspects, gestation and infancy, it ascends as</b> <b>feminine waters</b><sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">As explained previously, “feminine waters” refers to the “yearning” of lower levels for the light of higher levels. These lower levels are said to ascend to higher levels as “feminine waters,” flowing from below to above. In contrast, “masculine waters” refers to the flow of the supernal light from above to below. </i> <b>to the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>and brings</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>back</b> to the state of <b>“face-to-face.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">The ascent of feminine waters drives <i>Bina</i> to “turn toward” <i>Ḥokhma</i>. This means that <i>Bina</i> can now receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> through itself and pass that light to the level of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, the <i>partzuf</i> that was developed through the gestation and infancy phases here. This change in <i>Bina</i>, allowing it to transmit the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> was discussed in many previous sections of this work.</i> <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Bina</i> <b>then give the illumination to the lower</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>, which lowers the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from the</b> apertures of the eyes <b>to its own place, i.e., to the</b> <b>mouth</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">This descent of <i>Malkhut</i> effectively “undoes” the effects of the second constriction, allowing the lower vessels to ascend and return to their place. Since all five vessels are then in the level, all five lights are able to be enclothed in the level as well. The addition of the higher lights of <i>neshama</i>, <i>ḥaya</i>, and <i>yeḥida</i> means the <i>partzuf</i> now has “brains,” as the author of the <i>Sulam</i> proceeds to explain.</i> <b>At this point, the three vessels,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, which fell due to the ascent of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, once again ascend to their</b> <b>level</b><b>, and the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>is completed with the five vessels</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, and with the five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>This is called the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>brains</b><b>, for the first three lights,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i> and <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, are called</b> <b>brains</b><b>. For example, after <i>Atik</i> receives in a complete manner the two aspects of gestation and infancy, which are the</b> <b>heights</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> and <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i>Atik</i> <b>returns and ascends as</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>, and returns the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that are there</b> to the state of <b>face-to-face. Since the</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that is in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i> <b>is not intermingled with the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, therefore, when <i>Atik</i> receives this illumination it also brings down its own</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from its own</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">The turning of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Bina</i> of <i>Sag</i> toward each other causes changes in the lower levels The exposure of lower level (<i>Atik</i>) to the illumination of the level of <i>Sag</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> causes <i>Malkhut</i> to descend from the position it acquired in the level of <i>Bina</i> through the second constriction. This is because lower levels are imprinted by and conform to higher levels. Since the second constriction only begins in the level of <i>Nekudim</i>, below <i>Sag</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, exposure to the illumination of that higher, unconstricted level causes the lower level to copy the higher one, undoing the constriction caused by the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i>.</i> <b>Then</b> <i>Atik</i> <b>raises the three vessels, its</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, to its</b> <b>level</b><b>, which fell due to the intermingling of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">In the second constriction.</i> <b>It now has</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, of the vessels, in which the</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i> <b>of the lights can be</b> <b>enclothed</b><b>.</b>

Chapter 78

78. <b>When these</b> <b>brains</b> <b>emerge for the first time, a dispute arises between the right and the left (as explained at length in sections 29 – 30, above). For the left line, which is the bearer of the illumination of</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, wants to negate the right line, which is the bearer of the illumination of</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>. Due to this dispute, and this beating of right and left</b> against each other<b>, which occurs in these</b> <b>brains</b><b>, they are called “the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the back.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">As in the previous section , when discussing the dynamics of conflict and harmony between different aspects of the system, the author of the <i>Sulam</i> refers to positions of “face-to-face” and “ back-to-back.” Since these brains are in conflict (as explained more fully in sections 29 – 30 as well as in the surrounding sections there), they are called “brains of the back,” with the right and left failing to work in harmony to provide illumination to the lower level. </i> <b>The three aspects,</b> g<b>estation, infanc</b>y and <b>the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the back, have</b> now <b>been explained.</b>

Chapter 79

79. <b>This beating of left and right causes the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>to return to raising the</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>to the upper</b> level<sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">The conflict between the left and right lines (the left and right lines discussed in the earlier sections regarding the rectification of lines) means that the lower level does not receive any illumination from the upper level. As a result, it ascends again as feminine waters to trigger another change in the upper level, leading to the rectification of lines required for the illumination.</i><b>. For the illumination of the left, which is the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">See section 20 and subsequent sections for the in-depth discussion of the lines and their rectification.</i> <b>strikes and purifies all the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>in the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>, until the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>returns to as pure a state as it was in the first time it ascended to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <b>level</b><b>. That is, only the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root remains in it, and the remnant of</b> <b>enclothing</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, for by means of this equating it becomes attached to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>.</b> Then, <b>after</b> the partition <b>is</b> again <b>incorporated in the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the upper</b> <b>head</b><b>,</b> the partition <b>again receives a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>from the</b> <b>supernal light</b><b>, on the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root and the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>enclothing</b><b>, which were renewed in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>. The</b> <b>height</b> <b>of “three within three” again emerges upon</b> the partition<b>, which is the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>that is</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>within the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and which is called “the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of gestation” (as stated in section 75, above).</b><sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">This process is a repetition of the process described above in section 75. The phases of gestation, infancy and brains are duplicated. The final result is different in this second iteration, however, as will be explained. </i> <b>It has</b> now <b>been explained that the beating of the left upon the right, which occurred in the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the back,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">See section 78 above and the footnote there for the explanation of this concept. </i> <b>caused the return of the</b> lower <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>to the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>to receive a renewed aspect of gestation from the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>.</b>

Chapter 80

80. Then, <b>after</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>receives a renewed aspect of gestation, it returns and emerges from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>and</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. By means of this</b> <b>enclothing</b><b>,</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>again draws the lights from the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">The lower <i>partzuf</i> activates illumination from the upper one, as in the first round of gestation, infancy and brains described in the preceding sections.</i> <b>These lights</b> of <b>this drawing</b> of light <b>bring down the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root to the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">As in the previous round of gestation, infancy and brains, the drawing of the lights of the upper <i>partzuf</i> leads to the descent of the partition from the “forehead” of the head of the upper <i>partzuf</i> down to the “aperture of the eyes” of the head of the upper <i>partzuf</i>. This means the partition transitions from having a level of opacity of the root (associated with the forehead, the <i>Keter</i>) to opacity of the first level (associated with the aperture of the eyes, the <i>Ḥokhma</i>).</i> <b>That is, it brings down the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Malkhut</i> has a partition resting on it. Thus, a “descent of the partition“ means that the level of <i>Malkhut</i> and its partition have descended.</i> <b>from the forehead to the</b> apertures of the eyes<b>, and then the complete</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>emerges upon the</b> <b>partition</b><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">Once the partition possesses opacity of the first level, it engages in a fusion through collision that generates a height of <i>ruaḥ</i>, just like in the first round of gestation and infancy. This height of <i>ruaḥ</i> is the vessels and light of the gestated level of <i>Ḥesed</i>, <i>Gevura</i> and <i>Tiferet</i> that have now emerged in the phase of infancy.</i> <b>which is considered the spreading out of</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>from within</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>(as stated in section 76, above).</b> The lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>thus attains a new aspect of infancy, which is the mystical meaning of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 81

81. Then, <b>after</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>attains renewed gestation and infancy, it again ascends as</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>to the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>. The</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>accomplishes this ascension independently, since by leaving its root attached to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>(as stated in section 67), it can return there whenever necessary, and unite the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>that are there</b> into a state of <b>face-to-face (as will be explained in section 83, below).</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> then <b>give</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>the illumination that brings down the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from the</b> apertures of the eyes <b>to its place. As a result,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>ascend and attach to</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>as before, and</b> the lower <i>partzuf</i> <b>attains</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, of the vessels, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>of the lights.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote">Until this point, the second iteration of gestation, infancy and brains is the same as the first. Now the process reaches the point in which it was obstructed by the conflict between the left and right lines. In this iteration, that problem will now be solved, allowing for the illumination of <i>Ḥokhma</i> in the light of giving to reach the lower levels.</i>
<b>And in order that the dispute between right and left should not arise again, the middle line rises from below and unites the right and left so that they will illuminate together, with the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left</b> <b>enclothed</b> <b>in the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>in the right, and the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>in the right incorporated in the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the left (as explained in section 37, above). Then the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>illuminate in all their perfection, at which stage they are called “the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the front.” It has</b> now <b>been explained how, as a result of the conflict between the right and left of the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the back, the three aspects of gestation, infancy and the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the face, emerge again.</b>

Chapter 82

82. <b>Therefore, no</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>is complete until after it receives gestation</b>, <b>infancy and</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the back, and gestation, infancy and the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the front. For on account of the additional purification of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, until</b> it reaches <b>the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root, the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>can only receive their ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>through three consecutive phases, which are called gestation, infancy</b> and <b>brains</b> <b>(as stated in section 72, above). And since, in the first emergence of the</b> <b>brains</b>, <b>the beating of the right and left occurs, until the left purifies all the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, consequently, all the illuminations of gestation, infancy</b> and <b>brains</b> <b>which</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>received, depart. For with the loss of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>is negated and the lights depart, and the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>returns to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i> <b>for gestation, and it receives a renewed “three within three.”</b><sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the preceding sections, 76 and 79.</i> <b>It is subsequently born and receives a renewed infancy which brings down the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>from the forehead to the eyes, and the</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>emerge from</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i><b>, and</b> the <i>partzuf</i> <b>receives a renewed height of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>. It then ascends as</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>and it receives renewed</b> lights of <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, in which there already exists the middle line that unites the right and the left together – which are called “the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the front” – and then they illuminate and persist. Thus, until the</b> <i>partzufim</i> <b>attain the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>for the second time, they cannot persist.</b>

Chapter 83

<b>Face and Back, and Face-to-Face</b><br>83. <b>Even when the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>has already received the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the front, as stated above,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote">See the previous two sections.</i> <b>the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>which are there are still in a state of “face” and “back.” This means that only the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>receives the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the face.</b> With regard to <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, however, which is always in the</b> state of the <b>mystical meaning of the verse “for He delights in mercy,” as it wants</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>rather than</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, for this reason</b> <i>Bina</i> <b>is considered to have its “back” to</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and</b> <i>Bina</i> <b>does not want to receive the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the face from</b> <i>Ḥokhma</i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote">Since <i>Bina</i> seeks the light of giving, it does not receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> except as a conduit for <i>Ḥokhma</i> to be transmitted below to <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. In many of the earlier sections, this dynamic is discussed in the context of the rectification of lines and the transmission of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> through <i>Bina</i> to the lower levels.</i> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are always positioned in this state of “face” and “back,” until</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>ascends to them as</b> <b>feminine waters</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">256</sup><i class="footnote">This yearning of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> for the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> triggers <i>Bina</i> to “face” <i>Ḥokhma</i> and receive the flow of light in order to pass it through to <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>.</i> <b>Since there is a connection between</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>of the direct light to give the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of the direct light</b><sup class="footnote-marker">257</sup><i class="footnote">This idea is expressed in the preceding footnote. <i>Bina</i> and <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> are connected in the flow of supernal (direct) light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>, in that <i>Bina</i> transmits this light to <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. Thus, when <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> ascends as feminine waters, this yearning triggers <i>Bina</i> to face <i>Ḥokhma</i> to receive the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> on behalf of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>. However, as explained, <i>Bina</i> does not truly receive this light, but only transmits it.</i> <b>(as explained in <i>“Petiḥa LeḤokhmat HaKabbala</i>,” section 5) – therefore, when</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>ascends as</b> <b>feminine waters</b> <b>to</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>immediately turns her face back to</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>to receive from it the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the face – which are the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>– for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. This is just as</b> <i>Bina</i> <b>does in the five</b> <b>level</b><b>s of the direct light. It is then recognized that the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>has reached</b> a state of <b>“face-to-face” with</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 84

<b>Who Measures the</b> <b>Level</b> <b>in</b> <b>Atzilut</b><b>?</b> <br>84. <b>The following question arises: Since the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>contains only the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the root,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">258</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in previous sections, this level of opacity generates returning light for a <i>partzuf</i> of the level of <i>Malkhut</i>, the lowest level. Thus, the question here is, how could this low-opacity partition ultimately give rise to a full set of five <i>partzufim</i> in <i>Atzilut</i> or <i>Nekudim</i>?</i> <b>known as “forehead,” which has only the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of the light of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>, what has caused the emergence of five</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, namely <i>Atik</i>, </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>, <i>Abba </i>and <i>Imma</i>, and <i>Ze’er </i>and</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">259</sup><i class="footnote">These are the five <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>. Like all sets of five <i>partzufim</i>, each corresponds to one of the five main <i>sefirot</i>, <i>Keter</i> (<i>Atik</i>), <i>Ḥokhma</i> (<i>Arikh Anpin</i>), <i>Bina</i> (<i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>), <i>Tiferet</i> (<i>Ze'er Anpin</i>) and <i>Malkhut</i> (<i>Nukba</i>).</i> <b>in which <i>Atik</i> is the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>is the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>,</b> <b><i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i></b> <b>is the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>, and</b> <i><b>Ze’er </b></i><b>and <i></i></b><i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>is the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>? The same difficulty also applies to the world of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>: Since only the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is called the</b> “<b>apertures of the eyes,” is left in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, how could five</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>emerge in</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>?</b>

Chapter 85

85. <b>The answer is that the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>additionally became attached to the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>and the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, from the force of the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that ascended to the <i>nekudot</i> (vowels)</b><sup class="footnote-marker">260</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to one of four aspects of the level of <i>Sag</i> (or any given level), represented by the four aspects of the Hebrew alphabet: the <i>otiot</i> (written letter forms), the <i>tagin</i> (written crowns on the letters), the vowels (<i>nekudot</i>) of the letters and the <i>ta'amim</i> (the notes for chanting the letters when reading). The aspect of <i>nekudot</i> corresponds to the level of <i>Bina</i> in a given level.</i> <b>of the</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i> level <b>of</b> <i><b>Adam Kadmon</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">261</sup><i class="footnote">Once <i>Malkhut</i>, the “fourth level,” ascended to <i>Bina</i> in the second constriction (which took place from <i>Nekudim</i> and below), the partitions below this constriction received the opacity of <i>Malkhut</i> irrespective of their natural opacity. This can be thought of as <i>Malkhut</i> being present in every area below the level in which the second constriction transpires. </i> <b>For if the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>had not participated in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>in</b> <i>Nekudim</i> and <i>Atzilut</i><b>, no</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>could have emerged upon the</b> <b>partition</b><b>. For even the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the first</b> <b>level</b> <b>in</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>is considered a weak "gaze,"</b><sup class="footnote-marker">262</sup><i class="footnote">Often, the light that emerges from the “eyes” (the “aperture” of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i>) is referred to as “sight” or “gaze.”</i> <b>such that the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>does not produce any</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>from it.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">263</sup><i class="footnote">Such a small measure of opacity means that a structure of returning light and a subsequent <i>partzuf</i> cannot be properly formed.</i> <b>This is even more the</b> case with regard to <b>the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the forehead</b><sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote">Since this is the root level of opacity, which is even less capable of producing the requisite structures for a <i>partzuf</i>.</i> <b>in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, which is unfit for a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>to produce a</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i><b>. But as a result of the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>becoming attached to those</b> <b>partitions</b><b>, they become fit for a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>.</b>
<b>One should not ask: If so, shouldn’t a</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>have emerged upon the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, since the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>is attached to the</b> <b>partition</b><b>?</b><sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote">Since the fourth level is attached to the partition, shouldn't the opacity of the fourth level within it give rise to a <i>partzuf</i> of the level of <i>Keter</i>?</i>

Chapter 86

86. <b>The answer is that the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>produces a</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>only when it is situated in the place of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>, as then the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>that ascends from the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>upon</b> the partition<b>,</b> <b>enclothes</b> <b>the five vessels</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>with the five lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>. However, if the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>stands in the place of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, where there are only four vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>, the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>draws out only four lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>neshama</b></i> and <i><b>ḥaya</b></i><b>, in the four vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> and <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote">In other words, it is not only the opacity in the partition that determines the height of the emergent <i>partzuf</i>, but also the positioning of the partition. </i>
Similarly, <b>if the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>stands in the place of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, where there are only three vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> and <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, the</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>draws out only three lights,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> and <i><b>neshama</b></i><b>. And if the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>stands in the place of the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, where there are only two vessels,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>and</b><i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, its</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>draws out only</b> the <b>two lights</b> of <i><b>nefesh</b></i> and <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>. And so it was in</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, where the fusion occurred in the apertures of the eyes, which is the vessel of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and therefore only the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> and <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>emerged in</b> the phase of <b>immaturity</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">267</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in several of the preceding sections, the phase in which the partition is positioned at this higher point is a phase of immaturity, since the other lights (the “brains“) cannot be present.</i>
<b>And if the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>stands in the place of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, where there is only one vessel, its</b> <b>returning light</b> <b>draws out only one light,</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>. And so it was in</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>, as only the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i> <b>emerged in the gestation</b> phase<b>, as stated above, since the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>was in the place of the forehead, which is the vessel of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">268</sup><i class="footnote">As explained previously, the “forehead” is the part of the head of the upper <i>partzuf</i> that corresponds to the level of <i>Keter</i>, representing the level of <i>gulgalta</i>.</i> <b>However, after the drawing of the illumination</b> in the phase of infancy<b>, which pushed the fourth</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">269</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the aspect of <i>Malkhut</i>, the “fourth level” described in the previous section as having ascended to the <i>nekudot</i> aspect of <i>Sag</i> in the second constriction and bestowing opacity on the partitions below it. </i> from its location at the forehead <b>to the place of the first</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is called the</b> apertures of the eyes<b>, the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i> <b>emerged. Subsequently, through the illumination of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> and <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> in a state of <b>face-to-face, of the upper</b> <i>partzuf</i><b>, which brought down the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>to its place, to</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>– which raises the fallen</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">270</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in previous sections, when <i>Malkhut</i> is in its ascended state, the lower vessels of a given level are cut off from <i>Ḥokhma</i> and <i>Keter</i> of their level and descend to the level below. They return when the brains of the face of are activated, allowed <i>Malkhut</i> to descend to its place and these lowered vessels to ascend. </i> <b>to their</b> <b>level</b> <b>– there are five vessels once again,</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i> <b>and</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i><b>.
