Then the fourth</b> <b>level</b> <b>produces the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i> <b>with the light of</b> <i><b>yeḥida</b></i><b>, and this is the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of <i>Atik</i> of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i><b>.</b>

Chapter 87

87. <b>We must now explain how the other</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> of <i>Atzilut</i> <b>emerged, those which are below <i>Atik</i>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">271</sup><i class="footnote">As discussed frequently in the preceding sections, this is the first <i>partzuf</i> of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i>
<b>The idea is that initially, after the breaking of the vessels,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">272</sup><i class="footnote">This is a process that takes place in the level of <i>Nekudim</i>, ultimately leading to the formation of the <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.</i> <b>the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>ascended to the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>. That is, it was purified from all</b> <b>level</b><b>s of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>that emerged from it as the five</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">273</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the five <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Nekudim</i> that had already emerged from the opacity of the partition of <i>Nekudim</i>. Now that partition, having been purified of its opacity through the formation of the <i>partzufim</i> and the beating of the surrounding light against the partition in the standard process of <i>partzufim</i> formation discussed previously, ascends to the head of <i>Sag</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. As usual, this ascent is the result of an equating of form, in which the partition of <i>Nekudim</i> is now spiritually identical to the partition of the head of <i>Sag</i>.</i> <b>until it was equated with the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>. Nevertheless, the remnants of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the five</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>that emerged from</b> the partition <b>remained in</b> the partition<b>, apart from the last</b> <b>level</b><b>, which was lost, as has been explained in connection with all the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">274</sup><i class="footnote">When partitions are purified and then ascend to the partition of the head, where their opacity is “reawakened,” the last level remains permanently eroded. This was discussed in the extensive processes of <i>partzuf</i> formation detailed in the earlier sections of this work, sections 63–65.</i> <b>Therefore, when</b> the partition of <i>Nekudim</i> <b>was incorporated in the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>, the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of all five</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>was renewed in the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, and then a</b> <b>fusion through collision</b> <b>took place upon the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>.</b>
<b>However, not all</b> <b>level</b><b>s of the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>were included in the</b> <b>fusion through collision</b><b>, but only</b> the partition's <b>uppermost</b> <b>level</b><b>, which is the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the forehead that was attached to the fourth</b> <b>level</b><sup class="footnote-marker">275</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in the previous section, the fourth level of the <i>sefirot</i>, <i>Malkhut</i>, is now present in this context as a result of the second constriction. This presence gives rise to the capacity for fusion through collision against this partition.</i> <b>and by means of the three phases, gestation, infancy</b> and <b>brains</b><b>,</b> the <i>partzuf</i>’s <b>ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>were completed at the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">276</sup><i class="footnote">As usual, given that the opacity in the partition is that of the fourth level (the “most dense” level of opacity), the partition generates returning light of the height of <i>Keter</i>, and a <i>partzuf</i> of that height.</i> <b>The other remnants, from the rest of the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i> <b>that were in the</b> <b>partition</b><b>, did not receive anything from this</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>, since they were below the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><b>, and are</b> thus considered <b>immaterial in</b> relation to <b>its worth.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">277</sup><i class="footnote">The lower levels of opacity are inconsequential in comparison to the fourth level and are not manifest in the fusion through collision as a result.</i> <b>Consequently, when <i>Atik</i> emerged from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Sag</b></i><b>, all the remnants from the rest of the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i><b>, which were not incorporated in its</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision<b>, descended with it. After <i>Atik</i> was completed through the gestation, infancy and</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of the face, the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>illuminated upon the upper</b> <b>level</b> <b>of the remnants that remained in</b> the partition<b>, which is the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">278</sup><i class="footnote">Now that the fourth level of opacity has been activated and manifest as the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Atik</i>, the third level of opacity is the “most dense” level present. </i> <b>Through the three phases of gestation, infancy and</b> <b>brains</b><b>, ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>emerged, and this is the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">279</sup><i class="footnote">As discussed, this is the second <i>partzuf</i> of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>, corresponding to the level of <i>Ḥokhma</i> in the <i>sefirot</i>. This height emerges from a partition in which the opacity of the third level interacts with supernal light in a fusion through collision.</i>
<b>Here too, all the remnants of</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>that are less</b> opaque <b>than the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b> <b>are</b> considered <b>immaterial in</b> relation to <b>the value of the</b> <b>fusion</b> through collision <b>of the third</b> <b>level</b><b>, which emerged in the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of <i>Atik</i>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">280</sup><i class="footnote">As above, in order for a new <i>partzuf</i> to emerge, the partition of the previous level of opacity must be purified of its opacity at which time it ascends back to the head of the <i>partzuf</i>. There, the remnants of opacity are “reawakened,” except for the level that gave rise to the preceding <i>partzuf</i>, as that level has been permanently purified. Thus, the phrase “emerged in the head of <i>Atik</i>” refers to the phase of the process in which the new <i>partzuf</i> emerges from the partition as a result of the fusion through collision in the head of the preceding <i>partzuf</i> (<i>Atik</i> in this case). </i> <b>Therefore, when </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i> <b>was born and left from the</b> <b>head</b> <b>of <i>Atik</i> to its place, all those remnants were drawn with it to its place. After </b><i><b>Arikh Anpin</b></i><i> <b></b></i><b>was completed through all three phases, gestation, infancy and <i></i></b><b>brains</b><b>, the</b> <b>supernal light</b> <b>illuminated upon the uppermost</b> <b>level</b> <b>that remained in those remnants, which is the</b> <b>opacity</b> <b>of the second</b> <b>level</b><b>. Then, by means of the three aspects of gestation, infancy and</b> <b>brains</b><b>, ten</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>height</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>emerged upon it, and these are the</b> <i><b>partzuf</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Abba </b></i><b>and <i>Imma</i>.<i></i></b><sup class="footnote-marker">281</sup><i class="footnote">This is the term for the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> corresponding to the level of <i>Bina</i>.</i> <b>The rest of the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>emerged in the same manner. It has</b> now <b>been explained how the</b> <i><b>partzufim</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Atzilut</b></i> <b>emerged from one another.</b>

Chapter 88

<b>Two States of</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <br>88. <b>The</b> <i>sefira</i> of <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is the mystical meaning of the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">282</sup><i class="footnote">As this section explains, this term refers to the <i>partzuf</i> of <i>Nukba</i> which corresponds to the <i>sefira</i> of <i>Malkhut</i>. </i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>.</b> The root of <i>Nukba</i> <b>starts from</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>of the</b> <b>second constriction</b><b>, which concluded the seven</b> <i><b>sefirot</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">283</sup><i class="footnote">The phase of immaturity of <i>Nekudim</i> is the phase resulting from the ascent of <i>Malkhut</i> to <i>Bina</i> in the second constriction. The <i>Nukba</i> <i>partzuf</i> is at the “bottom” of the system of <i>partzufim</i> of <i>Nekudim</i> (and other corresponding levels). </i> <b>of the</b> <b>immaturity</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>.</b> This <i>Nukba</i> <b>is a separate</b> <b>level</b> <b>from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, as</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>includes</b> <i><b>Ḥesed</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Gevura</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Tiferet</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Netzaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Hod</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>, and the</b> <b>level</b> <b>below it is the</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>that concludes the</b> <i><b>Nekudim</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">284</sup><i class="footnote">The level of <i>Nukba</i>.</i> <b>Therefore, this</b> <i><b>Malkhut</b></i> <b>is considered a separate</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and a</b> <b>level</b> <b>below</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>There is also a different</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">285</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph explains the other “type” of <i>Nukba</i>. From <i>Nekudim</i> and downward, and as a result of the second constriction, each <i>partzuf</i> has a “male” and “female” aspect. Thus, <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> has a “left side,” the “female” aspect, which is the version of <i>Nukba</i> that is within the level of <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>.</i> that is <b>in the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. The left side of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is considered</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>’s <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, but this</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>is regarded as</b> part of <b>the actual</b> <b>body</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>since</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>is the mystical meaning of the middle line,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">286</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the “middle line” discussed in the earlier sections about the rectification of lines. The middle line ascends as feminine waters, a “yearning from below,” triggering changes in the levels above to allow the flow of the light of <i>Ḥokhma</i> to reach <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> and the levels below.</i> <b>which receives from the two lines, right and left, of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. The right of</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>receives from the right line of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is the mystical meaning of the</b> <b>light of giving</b><b>, and is considered the male side of</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>, while the left of</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>receives from the left line of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, which is the mystical meaning of the light of</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and is considered the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">287</sup><i class="footnote">The term “<i>Nukba</i>“ here refers both to the <i>Nukba</i> aspect within <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>, as well as the literal meaning of “female.”</i> <b>side of</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>. Nevertheless, they are both</b> part of <b>a single</b> <b>level</b><b>, and are incorporated into one another.</b>
<b>For it is known that initially there was the sun and the moon, which is the mystical meaning of the separate</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, with</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, as in “the two great lights” (Genesis 1:16; see <i>Ḥullin</i> 60a).</b> In that initial state, <b>the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>was an equal</b> <b>level</b> <b>to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and large like</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>. But then the moon – which is the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> that is <b>separate from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>– complained, saying: “It is impossible for two kings to use a single crown.” She was subsequently told: “Go and diminish yourself,” and was formed in the mystical meaning of “the lesser light.”</b>
<b>You thus find two states here, with regard to the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. One state is when</b> <i>Nukba</i> <b>was with</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, the state of the two great lights, when</b> <i>Nukba</i> <b>was equal to</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. The second state is after the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>was diminished and was formed in the mystical meaning of the lesser light (Genesis</b> 1:16<b>).</b>
<b>The meaning</b> of this <b>is as follows: When the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> that is <b>separate from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>was initially established, the Creator connected it with the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the mystical meaning of the left side of</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>, as stated above, and together they became a single</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>for</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. When the</b> <b>brains</b> <b>of right and left were drawn for</b> these aspects of <i>Nukba</i> <b>from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>– which is the mystical meaning of the right within</b> <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b> – took the lights of the right of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>. The</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> that is <b>separate</b> from <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>took the lights of the left of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, like the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>body</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, since</b> the separate <i>Nukba</i> <b>had become attached to</b> the <i>Nukba</i> in the body of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>into one</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>.</b>
<b>You already know that the lights of the right line of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are the</b> lights of <b>giving</b><b>, whereas the lights of the left line of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>are</b> the lights of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>. It thus turns out that</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>received the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>of the right of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>without</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, while the separate</b> <b>Nukba</b> <b>received the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i> <b>without</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>. Since, as is known,</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>cannot illuminate without</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>, the</b> <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>was therefore frozen in</b> the separate <i>Nukba</i><b>, and it became darkness and not light. This is the mystical meaning of the moon’s complaint, when it said that two kings cannot use a single crown. For when they both use a single crown, which is</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, that is considered</b> <i><b>Keter</b></i><sup class="footnote-marker">288</sup><i class="footnote">Since <i>Bina</i> of that level serves as the portal for the lights of <i>Ḥokhma</i> and giving, it is <i>Keter</i> for them, the portal to the higher supernal lights.</i> <b>for them,</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>becomes</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>without</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>becomes</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>without</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>, which is darkness, and</b> <i>Nukba</i> <b>could not withstand that state.</b>
<b>One should not ask: “Surely</b> it is the case that <b>before the separate</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>became attached to the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>body</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>, the right</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>, which is the male, was likewise receiving</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>, and the left</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>, which is the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in its</b> <b>body</b><b>, was receiving</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and yet the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i>’s <b>body</b> <b>could withstand it and was not darkness!” The explanation is that the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>body</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i> <b>is the</b> actual <b>self of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and therefore the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>within</b> this <i>Nukba</i> <b>is not separate from the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>in</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. This is not the case for the separate</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>, which is truly a different</b> <b>level</b> <b>from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, but since it became attached to the</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i> <b>in the</b> <b>body</b> of <i>Ze’er Anpin</i><b>,</b> the separate <i>Nukba</i> <b>received the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>of the left of</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, like</b> the <i>Nukba</i> in the body<b>. Consequently, after</b> the separate <i>Nukba</i> <b>received the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>within itself, the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>was separated from the</b> light of <b>giving</b><b>, as it has no connection to the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. The first state of the separate</b> <b>Nukba</b> <b>has thus been thoroughly explained.</b>
<b>Thus,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">289</sup><i class="footnote">Here the author of the <i>Sulam</i> returns to the quoted parable from the Talmud regarding the change in the relationship between the moon and the sun.</i> <b>in order that</b> the <i>Nukba</i> <b>could illuminate to the lower ones, she was told: “go and diminish yourself,” that is, that she should diminish herself from that great degree where she was equal to the</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>and receiving from</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>.</b><sup class="footnote-marker">290</sup><i class="footnote">As explained above, until this point, the separate <i>Nukba</i> was on the same level as <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> receiving light from <i>Bina</i>.</i> <b>Instead,</b> the separate <i>Nukba</i> <b>should descend to below</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, as she was at her root, which is below the entire</b> <b>level</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, and to receive all her lights from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. Since she</b> then <b>receives her lights from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, which is the mystical meaning of the middle line, the</b> light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>that</b> <i>Ze'er Anpin</i> <b>gives her is incorporated in the</b> light of <b>giving</b> <b>and she can illuminate</b> to the levels below<b>. This is the second state of the separate</b> <i><b>Nukba</b></i><b>. That which she received in the first state is considered the</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>neshama</b></i> <b>of the back,</b><sup class="footnote-marker">291</sup><i class="footnote">As in the preceding sections, the “illumination of back” implies a blockage preventing the flow of supernal light from continuing to lower levels, while “illumination of the face” indicates a functional structure allowing flow.</i> <b>meaning that they do not illuminate, whereas that which she receives in the second state is considered the</b> <i><b>nefesh</b></i><b>,</b> <i><b>ruaḥ</b></i><b>,</b> and <i><b>neshama</b></i> <b>of the face, meaning that they illuminate in their fullness. In order to understand this matter completely, you must study the <i>Zohar</i>, <i>Bereshit</i> I, in the article “The Two Great Lights,” 111–116, and <i>Idra Rabba</i>, in the article “<i>HaNesira</i>,” 23–25.</b>
<b>There are certain</b> ways in which <i>Nukba</i>'s <b>first state</b> is <b>superior, as then the</b> <b>level</b> <b>above her is</b> <i><b>Bina</b></i><b>, from which she can receive</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, and she does not need to receive from</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>. However, she cannot illuminate to the lower ones, on account of the lack of</b> the light of <b>giving</b><b>, as stated above, and therefore she is considered to be in the state of “</b>having her <b>back</b> turned<b>.” By contrast, in the second state, after</b> <i>Nukba</i> <b>has been diminished to below the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i><b>, she is no longer fit to receive</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i><b>, as the</b> <b>partition</b> <b>of</b> <i><b>Yesod</b></i> <b>of</b> <i><b>Ze’er Anpin</b></i> <b>blocks her, and she is compelled to receive</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>in the vessels of the back that remained in her from the first state. There are</b> likewise <b>certain</b> ways in which <b>the second state is superior to the first state, since then she can illuminate both</b> the light of <i><b>Ḥokhma</b></i> <b>and</b> the light of <b>giving</b> <b>to the lower</b> levels<b>, which is not the case in the first state, when she cannot illuminate to the lower</b> levels<b>.</b>
